### §2.4 `M06-D` — Cruelty/Ruthlessness

_Character disposition of merciless destructiveness._

1. Terms in sub-group (4): H6184 a.rits, H0394 akh.za.ri, H0393 akh.zar, H0395 akh.ze.riy.yut
2. Verse rows (33, deduped by term × location):

| Reference | Term | Status | Group | Set-aside reason | Spans in verse | Verse text |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Deu 32:33 | H0393 akh.zar | SA |  | the term functions as an intensifying descriptor of a physical quality (lethal potency of venom), not as a characteristic of inner being. | H2534 che.mah (rage) [poison]; H0393 akh.zar (cruel) [cruel] | Deu 32:33 their wine is the poison of serpents and the cruel venom of asps . |

## §3. Per-term comprehensive detail

Each term gets numbered sections: identity • meaning • anchor-verse linkages • groups • findings • pointers • auxiliary data. Verses are not repeated here — they are listed by sub-group in §2. Items linked only by registry are summarised here; exhaustive lists are in the appendix §4.

---

### H8130 sa.ne — to hate

**Identity & meaning**

1. Strong's: `H8130` · Lang: Hebrew · Owner: OWNER
2. Registry: R103 love · Legacy C-cluster: C17
3. Sub-group: `M06-A` (Hatred)
4. Term status: extracted · Evidential: — · Occurrences: 156

**Verses:** 139 distinct locations (see §2 for the verse table grouped by sub-group).

**Group memberships (2)**

| Group ID | Code | Description | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1601 | 550-001 | Term names hatred as the inner moral disposition opposed to love — God's righteous hatred of evil and injustice; human hatred of neighbour and brother as the mark of moral disorder; and the psalmist's holy hatred of evil aligned with God |  |
| 3590 | 550-002 | Term names hatred received from others — those who hate me, my enemies — hate as an inner-being disposition coming from another person, directed at the speaker / object | Created from M06 UT review v1 flag 1 (2026-05-06) |

**Findings — direct (Strong's mention) (3)**

| Finding ID | Type | Anchor verses | Excerpt |
|---|---|---|---|
| OBS-103-T2-017 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Lev 19:17, Pro 10:12, Jam 4:4 | The structural opposite is hatred (sane — H8130, 139 active verses, OWNER term, OBS-103-030). Sane is embedded in R103 as an OWNER term — the programme treats hate as constitutive of the love vocabulary's boundary, not external to it. Lev 19:17 ('you shall not hate your brother in your heart') places hate as the inner alternative to love of neighbour (OBS-103-114). Pro 10:12 ('hatred stirs up strife, love covers all offences,' OBS-103-097) places them as causal-opposite forces with opposed social effects. The secondary structural opposite at the ultimate level is enmity with God: friendship with the world is enmity (echthra) with God (Jam 4:4, OBS-103-058). But hatred is the primary inner-being opposite — it is the same inner mechanism as love (directed orientation) running in the opposed direction. |
| OBS-103-T2-113 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Lev 19:17, Psa 97:10, Pro 10:12 | Yes — embedded as OWNER. H8130 sane (to hate, 139 active / 156 total) is the structural opposite within the registry (OBS-103-030). H8131 sena (hating, 1 active) is a second form. The hate vocabulary is not XREF but OWNER — the programme treats the structural opposite as constituent of the love vocabulary's boundary (OBS-103-019). Additionally: the philo-compound negative forms (afilarguros — not-money-loving; pseudadelfos — false-brother) name the absence of specific love-forms. The disordered love vocabulary names love's distorted presence rather than its absence. True lovelessness (absence without misdirection) is not prominently named — the data suggests the inner mechanism is always present and always directed at something; the question is always the object, not the presence or absence of love-capacity. |
| SYN-INTER-103-015 | SYNTHESIS_INTER_TIER |  | The vocabulary evidence grounds the faculty claims with lexical precision. Identity faculty (T3.10): agapētos (person-type of being-loved), chasid (person-type of chesed), filos (person-type of phileō) — all three are lexically grounded person-type terms (Q&A-127). Moral sensitivity faculty (T3.8): the hate-vocabulary embedded as OWNER (H8130 sane — Q&A-126) grounds the claim that love requires and produces righteous hatred — the structural opposite provides the moral sensitivity calibration. Memory faculty (T3.3): the verb-form analysis (Q&A-123) shows that chesed as noun-primary form implies a dispositional quality that persists — memory is the chesed-noun's faculty correlate. Attention faculty (T3.1): phileō's etymology (from philos — friend) implies a relational salience structure — the one who is phileō-loved becomes salient to the lover's attention-field. The vocabulary's etymological structure (Q&A-122) is thus the lexical ground of the faculty engagement pattern: the root meanings point toward the faculties each term primarily activates. |

**Findings — via anchor verse (44 unique)**

| Finding ID | Type | Matched anchor refs | Excerpt |
|---|---|---|---|
| 112-F009 | VERSE_PATTERN | Psa 119:113 | Double-mindedness (dipsuchos/se.eph) documents inner division as a cross-testament pathology. James presents inner unity as a condition for receiving from God and for effective action; Ps 119:113 makes it a moral stance. |
| OBS-103-T2-017 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Lev 19:17 | The structural opposite is hatred (sane — H8130, 139 active verses, OWNER term, OBS-103-030). Sane is embedded in R103 as an OWNER term — the programme treats hate as constitutive of the love vocabulary's boundary, not external to it. Lev 19:17 ('you shall not hate your brother in your heart') places hate as the inner alternative to love of neighbour (OBS-103-114). Pro 10:12 ('hatred stirs up strife, love covers all offences,' OBS-103-097) places them as causal-opposite forces with opposed social effects. The secondary structural opposite at the ultimate level is enmity with God: friendship with the world is enmity (echthra) with God (Jam 4:4, OBS-103-058). But hatred is the primary inner-being opposite — it is the same inner mechanism as love (directed orientation) running in the opposed direction. |
| OBS-103-T2-018 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Lev 19:17 | 1Cor 13:4-7 provides the programme's most explicit catalogue of what love excludes: envy, boasting, arrogance, rudeness, self-seeking, irritability, resentfulness, rejoicing in wrongdoing (OBS-103-127). The list names love's resistances across moral, relational, and emotional registers. At the structural level, love resists division of ultimate allegiance (Jam 4:4 — cannot love God and world simultaneously, OBS-103-058), resists self-assertion as the primary orientation (love-of-self as the first item in the last-days catalogue, OBS-103-137), and resists the withholding of self (Joh 15:13 — love's maximum is the giving of the soul/life, OBS-103-125). Love also explicitly resists concealment of inner truth from the beloved: Lev 19:17 contrasts hate-as-silence with love-as-frank-correction (OBS-103-114). |
| OBS-103-T2-022 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Lev 19:17 | Yes — evidenced across several groups. Joh 15:15 (OBS-103-052): love's communicative mode is knowledge-disclosure — Jesus names the content of his friendship with the disciples as 'all that I have heard from my Father I have made known to you.' Love shares the inner world of the lover with the beloved. Lev 19:17 (OBS-103-114): frank correction (hocheach tochi'ach — honest rebuke) is love's communicative act, in contrast to hate's silence. The kiss (filēma, katafileō — OBS-103-054, OBS-103-056) is love's somatic-communicative mode — the body's expression of the inner word. The divine declaration ('this is my beloved Son' — Mat 3:17, OBS-103-120) is love's constitutive speech act: the naming of belovedness is itself the conferral of identity. Love therefore has a speech-mode that functions as: disclosure (sharing the inner world), correction (honest engagement), and declaration (constitutive naming). |
| OBS-103-T2-047 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Lev 19:17 | Indirect evidence only. The conscience (suneidēsis) does not appear by name in R103's anchor verses. However: Lev 19:17 (OBS-103-114) — the prohibition on hating the brother 'in your heart' and the command to rebuke frankly — implies conscience-engagement: the inner recognition that hate is wrong and that honest love requires action. 2Cor 11:26 (OBS-103-067) and Gal 2:4 (OBS-103-068) — the false brother's concealed inner orientation — implies conscience is involved in the recognition of inner deception. The programme's suneidēsis registry (R026) co-occurs with love at Rom 8:29 (shared anchor). Gap: conscience's specific engagement with love is not explicitly evidenced in R103's anchor corpus. The conscience-love connection is inferred from the moral imperative structure of the love commands. |
| OBS-103-T2-054 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Lev 19:17 | The indirect evidence suggests conscience and love operate at the same moral depth but through different mechanisms. The conscience recognises the moral wrongness of hate-in-the-heart (Lev 19:17, OBS-103-114); love is what the conscience directs the person toward as the alternative. If conscience is the inner moral monitor, love is the inner moral orientation — the conscience identifies what violates love; love provides the positive orientation the conscience is protecting. Gap: this relationship is inferred, not directly evidenced in R103's anchor verses. |
| OBS-103-T2-065 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Psa 97:10, Lev 19:17 | Yes — love is the primary shaper of moral sensitivity in the data. Psa 97:10 (OBS-103-115): 'O you who love the Lord, hate evil' — love of God directly produces moral sensitivity to evil (the capacity to hate what is wrong). Lev 19:17 (OBS-103-114): the prohibition on hating the brother in the heart implies that moral sensitivity recognises inner hate as morally significant. 1Cor 13:6 (within OBS-103-127): love 'does not rejoice in wrongdoing' — love shapes the moral sensitivity that recognises wrongdoing as something not to be celebrated. Pro 10:12 (OBS-103-097): love's moral sensitivity distinguishes between hatred-that-stirs-strife and love-that-covers — the faculty that makes this distinction is morally sensitised by love. Love functions as the moral-sensitivity calibrator: it determines what the inner person registers as morally significant and how they register it. |
| OBS-103-T2-066 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Lev 19:17 | The conscience-as-faculty relationship to love is addressed at T2.7 (Q&A-053, Q&A-062, Q&A-063). The additional faculty-dimension: the conscience functions as the internal monitor that activates when love's requirements are violated (hating the brother in the heart, Lev 19:17) or when love's form is distorted (false brotherhood, Gal 2:4). Love provides the positive standard; conscience provides the monitoring mechanism. The faculty-relationship: love is the norm; conscience is the norm-enforcer in the inner person. Gap: the direct conscience-love faculty interaction is not named in R103's anchor verses. The relationship is structurally inferred. |
| OBS-103-T2-079 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Pro 27:6 | Human-to-human love is the ethical core of the love commandment. The data shows it operating in five structural relationships: (a) **Neighbour** (H7453 rea — 173 active) — the primary OT ethical form: 'love your neighbour as yourself' (Lev 19:18); (b) **Enemy** (Mat 5:44, OBS-103-143) — the most demanding NT extension — love directed to those who actively oppose the person; (c) **Community of faith** (Joh 13:34, 1Th 3:12) — mutual love as the community's defining practice; (d) **Friendship** (filos, H0157H, dod vocabulary) — personal loyal love; (e) **Family** (filadelfia, filostorgos, filoteknos, filandros) — love within natural and spiritual family structures. The human-to-human direction is the most evidentially diverse — spanning obligation (neighbour-love), choice (friendship), natural bond (family), and cost (enemy-love). |
| OBS-103-T2-081 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Pro 19:7 | Breakdowns evidenced: (a) **False brotherhood** — Gal 2:4 (OBS-103-068): using the community-love structure to serve a contrary agenda — the most dangerous breakdown because it uses love's form; (b) **Betrayal-kiss** — Luk 22:48 (OBS-103-054): love's somatic sign (kiss) used to indicate enmity — betrayal as the weaponisation of love's language; (c) **Desertion for world-love** — 2Ti 4:10 (OBS-103-148): abandonment of love-community for love of world; (d) **Poverty-caused dissolution** — Pro 19:7 (OBS-103-073): friendship tested by adversity may fail when it was conditional; (e) **Pride-driven rivalry** — Luk 22:24 (OBS-103-131): love-of-primacy at the table of the Lord. Conditions for maintenance: honest engagement (Lev 19:17, frank rebuke), soul-purification (1Pe 1:22), shared suffering (1Pe 5:9). The most dangerous breakdown is false brotherhood — it operates inside the love-structure while working against it. |
| OBS-103-T2-113 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Lev 19:17, Psa 97:10 | Yes — embedded as OWNER. H8130 sane (to hate, 139 active / 156 total) is the structural opposite within the registry (OBS-103-030). H8131 sena (hating, 1 active) is a second form. The hate vocabulary is not XREF but OWNER — the programme treats the structural opposite as constituent of the love vocabulary's boundary (OBS-103-019). Additionally: the philo-compound negative forms (afilarguros — not-money-loving; pseudadelfos — false-brother) name the absence of specific love-forms. The disordered love vocabulary names love's distorted presence rather than its absence. True lovelessness (absence without misdirection) is not prominently named — the data suggests the inner mechanism is always present and always directed at something; the question is always the object, not the presence or absence of love-capacity. |
| OBS-103-T2-135 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Psa 97:10, Lev 19:17 | Yes — and the data makes this explicit. Psa 97:10 (OBS-103-115): 'O you who love the Lord, hate evil' — hatred of evil is commanded of those who love God. Righteous hatred is not love's failure but love's necessary complement: you cannot love God and be indifferent to what opposes him. Lev 19:17 (OBS-103-114): 'you shall not hate your brother in your heart' — hatred of the brother is wrong. The same inner-being mechanism (hatred as directed-aversion) can be rightly directed (at evil) or wrongly directed (at the brother). This is the precise structural parallel to love: love rightly directed (toward God and neighbour) vs love wrongly directed (toward money, pleasure, world). Hatred operates under the same moral logic as love: the mechanism is morally neutral; the object determines the moral quality. The ordered inner life requires both rightly directed love AND rightly directed hatred. |
| OBS-103-T2-156 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Psa 97:10, Lev 19:17 | Love **enables and calibrates** moral evaluation — it is the primary calibrator of the moral faculty's standards. Psa 97:10 (OBS-103-115): 'O you who love the Lord, hate evil' — love of God calibrates the moral evaluation that rightly identifies evil as what must be hated. Lev 19:17 (OBS-103-114): the prohibition on hating the brother 'in your heart' requires moral evaluation of inner states, not just outer acts — love enables the inner moral evaluation that reaches below behaviour to motivation. 1Cor 13:6 (within OBS-103-127): love 'does not rejoice in wrongdoing but rejoices with the truth' — love calibrates the moral evaluation faculty so that wrongdoing generates the correct response (non-rejoicing) and truth generates joy. Disordered love impairs moral evaluation: the Pharisees' love-of-money produced mockery of Jesus' teaching (Luk 16:14, OBS-103-136) — a distorted moral evaluation produced by a distorted love. |
| OBS-103-T2-157 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Psa 97:10 | The moral evaluation pattern reveals love as the moral faculty's primary standard-source. The person calibrated by love-of-God sees evil as evil and good as good (Psa 97:10) — the love-orientation determines the correctness of the moral evaluation. This means moral failure is often misdiagnosed: what looks like impaired moral faculty may be a disordered love-faculty — the person who evaluates wrongly does so because they love wrongly (Luk 16:14 — money-love produces moral mockery). The pattern implies that moral formation cannot proceed without love-formation: sharpening the moral faculty without reordering the love-faculty produces moralists who identify evil correctly but love wrongly. The data's architecture places love prior to moral evaluation: love → moral evaluation → right action, not moral evaluation → motivation → action. Love calibrates the evaluator before the evaluation occurs. |
| OBS-103-T2-158 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Lev 19:17 | From the available evidence: love appears to **enable** conscience by providing the standard against which conscience operates. Lev 19:17 (OBS-103-114) — 'do not hate your brother in your heart' — implies conscience is the faculty that registers the inner hate as moral failure; love is what conscience is protecting on behalf of. The conscience that has internalised love's requirements is the conscience that registers hate-in-the-heart as a violation. Conversely, disordered love may **impair** conscience: the money-lover (Luk 16:14, OBS-103-136) who ridicules Jesus' teaching has a conscience whose sensitivity to error is dulled by the competing love-object. Gap: the direct conscience-love relationship is inferred from indirect evidence. The suneidēsis vocabulary does not appear in R103's anchor verses. Partial answer. |
| OBS-103-T2-159 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Lev 19:17 | The indirect pattern suggests love and conscience are functionally complementary but operate at different constitutional levels. Love provides the positive orientation (toward the beloved, toward the good); conscience provides the negative monitor (detecting violations of that orientation). Together they constitute a complete moral inner-being system: love sets the direction; conscience enforces the boundaries. If this is accurate, love is what conscience is oriented to protect — the conscience registers violations of love's requirements (hate-in-the-heart, false-brotherhood, betrayal-kiss). Gap: the data cannot confirm this functional complementarity directly from named evidence. It is an inference from the structural juxtaposition of Lev 19:17 (hate-prohibition) and Lev 19:18 (love-command). Session D treatment required for confirmed resolution. |
| OBS-103-T2-166 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Pro 19:7 | All four — suffering deepens, tests, reveals, and produces love in the evidence. **Deepens:** the sufferer's appeal to love in affliction (Psa 63:3 — 'because your steadfast love is better than life' written by David in the wilderness) shows suffering deepening the value assigned to divine love. **Tests:** Pro 19:7 (OBS-103-073) — poverty dissolves conditional friendship; adversity-testing reveals which loves are genuine. Pro 27:6 (OBS-103-059): 'faithful are the wounds of a friend' — love expressed through painful honesty under pressure. **Reveals:** Joh 11:36 (OBS-103-149): Jesus' grief at Lazarus' tomb reveals his love — suffering-response is love's most visible evidence (grief = love under loss). 2Sa 1:26 (OBS-103-095): David's lament reveals the measure of his love for Jonathan. **Produces:** Luk 7:47 (via SD-020) — love produced through the suffering-and-forgiveness pathway: forgiveness of guilt-suffering generates love. The suffering-love relationship is reciprocal and multi-directional. |
| OBS-117-T2-086 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Gen 37:4 | Authentic peace deeply enables and deepens relational capacity. Evidence: (1) 1Ch 12:17 — the sha.lom-friendship produces heart-union; (2) Eph 2:14-16 — Christ's peace breaks down the "dividing wall of hostility" and creates one body from two peoples — peace is the engine of the most dramatic relational restoration in the NT; (3) Jer 29:7 — seeking the welfare of the exile city requires expanding relational capacity to include the former enemy's community; (4) 1Sa 25:6 (2511-001) — the greeting-blessing as an act of relational goodwill. Conversely: peacelessness impairs relational capacity — Gen 37:4 ("they hated him and could not speak peacefully to him") — the absence of sha.lom-orientation makes genuine relational connection impossible; Jer 20:10 (anshei sha.lom who betray) — false sha.lom destroys relational capacity through betrayal. The instruction note for T3.11 distinguishes characteristics that build/sustain connection from those that restore/repair it — this registry does both: shalom builds connection (friendship, greeting, covenant) and restores broken connection (Eph 2:14). |
| OBS-117-T2-098 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Gen 37:4 | Enabling conditions: (1) Receptivity — the quieted person is positioned to receive what the peaceful person extends (Psa 131:2 — the weaned-child posture of receptive calm); (2) Genuine seeking: 1Ch 12:17 — "if you have come to me in friendship to help me" — the intention that enables the sha.lom relationship is genuine orientation toward the other's good; (3) Non-hostility: Gen 37:4 — the brothers "could not speak peaceably to Joseph" because of hatred — hatred blocks peace-reception. Blocking conditions: (1) Hatred: Gen 37:4; (2) Stubbornness: Isa 30:15 — the stubborn heart refuses peace even when God offers it; human stubbornness would equally block human-to-human peace-reception; (3) False peace already in place: Deu 29:19 — the person who has self-generated false peace is not available to receive genuine peace from another because they believe they already have it. |
| OBS-060-T2-013 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Gen 29:33 | The data reveals a dual structure: faithfulness in this registry is simultaneously a disposition and an act. The inner-being disposition is the prior commitment or orientation (covenant faithfulness in 872-001, compassion in 872-002, inner trust in 872-005) from which the act of giving proceeds. The giving itself is the act — the enacted, external form of the inner disposition. Neither alone constitutes faithfulness as the data describes it: the disposition without the act remains unfulfilled commitment; the act without the disposition is mere transaction. The group landscape (OBS-060-025) confirms this: each group description names both an inner-being source (covenant faithfulness, love and compassion, inner orientation toward God) and an enacted expression (giving land, giving in response to need, self-giving). This is best described as a disposition-in-action: an inner-being quality that is only fully itself when expressed outwardly. This is consistent with DIM-60-001 (OBS-060-032, OBS-060-053). |
| OBS-060-T2-019 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Gen 29:33 | The data reveals five distinct operational modes (OBS-060-025, OBS-060-051). (1) Performative giving: the act of giving constitutes a covenantal reality — "I will give this land" enacts the covenant (OBS-060-016, OBS-060-036). (2) Responsive giving: giving triggered by the recipient's inner condition — God gives in direct answer to suffering/need (OBS-060-037). (3) Endowing giving: giving that deposits inner-being capacity — Spirit, wisdom, understanding given directly to the inner life (OBS-060-040, OBS-060-041). (4) Judicial giving: giving as moral consequence — giving-over as the expression of inner moral response to faithlessness (OBS-060-042, OBS-060-043). (5) Transformative giving: giving that reverses inner-being states — replacing depletion with fullness, mourning with gladness (OBS-060-048, OBS-060-049, OBS-060-050). In the human direction, a sixth mode is also present: (6) Relinquishing giving: releasing what was received, recognising divine sovereignty over all given goods (OBS-060-044). |
| OBS-060-T2-020 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Gen 29:33 | Yes — significantly so. By direction: divine giving (6 of 7 groups) operates from sovereign initiative and covenantal obligation; human giving (1 group, 872-005) operates from responsive orientation and trust. The operational logic differs: God gives as the originating party; the human gives as the responsive, image-bearing party. By context: performative giving (covenant ratification, Gen 15:18) operates as a speech-act constituting reality; responsive giving (Gen 29:33) operates as compassionate provision; judicial giving (Hos 13:11) operates as moral consequence; transformative giving (Isa 61:3) operates as eschatological reversal. By constitutional level: endowing giving (Neh 9:20, Job 38:36) operates at the spirit/cognitive level, depositing inner-being capacity; self-giving (Isa 50:6) operates through the body as the expression of inner disposition; glory-giving (Isa 42:8, Jer 13:16) operates at the relational-correspondence level between inner-being orientation and its proper object. |
| OBS-060-T2-023 | VERSE_PATTERN | Gen 29:33 | The immediate response varies by the mode of giving received. (1) Covenantal giving → worship/altar-building (Gen 12:7). (2) Compassionate giving (child given to Leah) → naming/attribution of divine hearing (Gen 29:33, OBS-060-037) — the name Simeon memorialises the inner act of divine hearing and giving. (3) Judicial giving-over → no inner-being response recorded in the anchor verses — the judicial act proceeds without a recorded human response in the primary texts. (4) Eschatological giving → restored responsiveness/praise (Hos 2:15, Isa 61:3). (5) Divine giving-and-taking → blessing-under-loss (Job 1:21). The variation is directionally consistent: where receiving is welcome, the response is worship/praise/gratitude; where receiving is judicial, there is silence on response (suggesting the human is the object, not the agent). The variation is meaningful, not random. |
| OBS-060-T2-028 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Gen 29:33 | The data provides partial evidence. For covenantal giving (872-001): the condition evidenced is being in a covenant relationship with God — the giving of land is addressed to Abraham and his offspring, not to all humanity indiscriminately. The covenant relationship is the precondition of reception. For compassionate giving (872-002): the condition evidenced is the presenting of genuine inner need — Leah is hated and suffering; God hears and gives (OBS-060-037). Expressed need or suffering appears to enable responsive giving. For eschatological giving (872-007): no precondition is named in the anchor verses — those who mourn receive beauty (Isa 61:3), suggesting mourning itself is the enabling condition. For human self-giving (Job 1:21, Isa 50:6): the enabling inner condition is trust/covenantal identity — Job's worship proceeds from recognising divine sovereignty; the Servant gives himself because he trusts divine vindication. Gap: the data does not address whether ongoing faithfulness or human moral condition affects the receptivity to divine covenantal giving — the texts name the giving as God's initiative, not as contingent on human merit. |
| OBS-060-T2-033 | MEANING_OBSERVATION | Gen 29:33 | Yes — four secondary dimensions are carried, each with substantial group-level evidence: (1) Relational Disposition (groups 872-002 and 872-005) — compassionate responsive giving (GOD) and self-giving as inner orientation (HUMAN). This dimension is the most quantitatively significant after Moral Character (30 + 19 = 49 relevant verses combined). (2) Cognition (group 872-003) — divine giving of inner-being capacities: Spirit, wisdom, understanding. (3) Divine-Human Correspondence (group 872-006) — glory-ascription in its proper directional structure. (4) Transformation (group 872-007) — eschatological reversal of inner states. These secondary dimensions do not compete with Moral Character as primary — they are distinct operational modes of the same characteristic, each revealing a different dimension of how inner-being giving functions in the biblical corpus. The DIM-60-SD001 pointer (OBS-060-033) identifies this dimensional breadth as a programme-level finding: na.tan illustrates that a single action-verb can carry the full breadth of inner-being dimensional engagement depending on context. |
| OBS-060-T2-054 | SPIRIT_SOUL_BODY | Gen 29:33 | Yes — the origin shifts across contexts as follows. In covenantal giving contexts (872-001): origin is divine internal character, unconditional and self-generated. In responsive giving (872-002): origin is divine compassion triggered by the human's presented need — the origin is still internal to God but responsive to external condition. In endowing giving (872-003): origin is divine initiative depositing capacity in the human — giving constitutes the human's inner capacity from the outside. In judicial giving-over (872-004): origin is divine moral response to human faithlessness — external condition (human behaviour) shapes the mode of divine giving. In human self-giving (872-005): origin is the human's inner trust and acceptance, formed by but distinct from received divine giving. The characteristic's origin is not static — it is context-sensitive across the seven groups, reflecting the full range of divine-human interaction. |
| OBS-060-T2-057 | OBSERVATION | Gen 29:33 | The hearing faculty is explicitly engaged in two instances. Gen 29:33 (OBS-060-037): "the Lord has heard (shama) that I am hated" — divine hearing is the perceptive act that precedes and grounds the compassionate giving. The perception of inner suffering is the precondition of the responsive giving. Neh 9:20 (OBS-060-040): God gives Spirit "to instruct them" — the Spirit-giving produces the capacity to hear/receive instruction, engaging the perceptive-receptive dimension at the cognitive-formative level. For the human direction: Jer 13:16 (OBS-060-047) — "before your feet stumble... while you look for light" — visual perception (looking for light) is present in the failure-to-give-glory context, though as the condition of the person who has not given glory rather than as a faculty engaged by giving itself. Hearing is the primary perceptive faculty engaged. |
| OBS-060-T2-059 | OBSERVATION | Gen 29:33 | The pattern reveals that this characteristic has a relational-perceptive architecture: inner-being giving is grounded in prior perception (God hears suffering before giving; Spirit-endowment enables the human to hear instruction) and it shapes subsequent perception (failure to give glory produces perceptive darkening; receiving eschatological giving restores responsiveness — Hos 2:15, OBS-060-050). The characteristic is not perception itself, but it operates through perception as both its precondition and its consequence. This reveals that inner-being giving is not blind action — it is responsive, attentive, and formative of the recipient's perceptive capacity. |
| OBS-060-T2-084 | OBSERVATION | Gen 29:33 | Yes — relational capacity is intrinsic to the characteristic. Every classified use of na.tan in the inner-being register involves a giver and a receiver in genuine relational engagement. Group 872-002 most directly engages relational capacity: God gives in direct response to Leah's inner condition of being hated (Gen 29:33, OBS-060-037) — this presupposes divine attentiveness to the relational situation of the other. Hos 11:8 (OBS-060-038) shows the relational depth of divine giving: the heart recoils, compassion grows warm — these are movements of genuine relational connection, not administrative decision. For the human: Isa 50:6 — the Servant's self-giving is an act of relational fidelity. Job 1:21 — the relinquishing blessing is addressed to the Lord (not internal) — it is a relational act toward God. Group 872-006 (glory-giving) is structurally about the proper orientation of the divine-human relational connection. |
| OBS-060-T2-086 | OBSERVATION | Gen 29:33 | The pattern reveals that this characteristic is constitutively relational — it cannot be abstracted from the two-party structure of giver and receiver. Every mode of inner-being giving in the registry is a relational act: covenantal commitment is always toward a covenantal partner; compassionate giving is always responsive to someone's condition; judicial giving-over is always addressed at a covenant relationship that has broken; glory-giving is always directional toward God. The characteristic builds, sustains, and — in its eschatological mode — restores relational capacity. This confirms the group 872-002 and 872-005 Relational Disposition dimension assignments and deepens the understanding of why the registry's dimensional breadth spans Moral Character and Relational Disposition: the characteristic is moral in its source (covenantal commitment) and relational in its expression (always enacted toward another). |
| OBS-060-T2-087 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Gen 29:33 | Yes — extensively and across five of seven groups. God gives covenantally toward Israel (872-001: land, promise, blessing — Gen 12:7, Gen 15:18); compassionately toward those in need (872-002: responsive giving to suffering — Gen 29:33, Hos 11:8 withheld giving-over); formatively toward the inner life (872-003: Spirit, wisdom, understanding — Neh 9:20, Job 38:36); judicially toward the faithless (872-004: giving-over as moral consequence — Hos 13:11, Jer 12:7); and transformatively toward the mourning (872-007: ashes → beauty, faint spirit → praise — Isa 61:3, Hos 2:15). Every mode of God-to-human giving is evidenced in the anchor verses. The God-to-human direction is the dominant directional structure of the registry (6 of 7 groups, OBS-060-017). |
| OBS-060-T2-088 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Gen 29:33 | The data reveals four distinct bases operating across the groups: (1) Covenantal (872-001): God gives because the covenant is in force — the giving enacts prior covenantal commitment, regardless of immediate merit. Gen 15:18 — the covenant ratification is the basis; the giving follows from it. Mal 2:5 — "my covenant with him was one of life and peace, and I gave them to him" — the giving is covenantal through and through. (2) Responsive (872-002): God gives in response to presented inner need — Leah's condition triggers divine hearing and giving (Gen 29:33). The basis is the creature's condition, perceived by divine attentiveness. (3) Formative (872-003): God gives Spirit/wisdom as constitutive endowment — the basis appears to be divine formative purpose for the person, not contingent on their current state. (4) Moral-consequential (872-004): God gives-over as moral response to faithlessness — the basis is moral consistency: the covenant is executed in both directions. (5) Eschatological-grace (872-007): God gives to the mourning without stated precondition — grace and eschatological initiative are the basis. No single basis covers all modes; the characteristic operates across a spectrum from pure grace to moral consequence. |
| OBS-060-T2-089 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Gen 29:33 | God's giving reveals a complex of inner-being dispositions toward the human person. (1) Covenantal commitment: God's giving of land and promise over generations reveals that his orientation toward Abraham and his offspring is one of binding, persistent faithfulness — a commitment that does not lapse with time or circumstance. (2) Attentive compassion: God hears Leah's inner condition and gives in response — his orientation is one of attentiveness to the inner suffering of the creature, not detachment. (3) Formative care: God gives Spirit and wisdom to equip the person for formation and service — his orientation is developmental, not merely transactional. (4) Moral seriousness: God gives-over in response to faithlessness — his orientation includes moral consistency and covenantal accountability. He is not sentimentally lenient. (5) Hos 11:8 holds all of these in tension: the heart that recoils in compassion is also the heart that had determined judgement — God's orientation is a complex of justice and compassion held together by sovereign grace. |
| OBS-060-T2-096 | OBSERVATION | Gen 29:33 | Yes — every group with God as subject shows the human receiving divine inner-being giving. Reception operates differently by mode: (1) Covenantal reception (872-001): the human receives the promise/land as participant in an inherited covenant — reception is identity-constituting. Abram receives the promise and immediately responds with worship (Gen 12:7, OBS-060-035). (2) Compassionate reception (872-002): Leah receives a child in direct response to her inner suffering — reception is responsive and experiential (Gen 29:33, OBS-060-037). (3) Formative reception (872-003): the human receives Spirit, wisdom, and understanding — reception is constitutive, forming inner capacity. (4) Eschatological reception (872-007): those who mourn receive beauty/gladness/praise — reception is transformative, replacing depleted inner states with new ones. The mode of reception corresponds directly to the mode of giving: the characteristic is received as it is given. |
| OBS-060-T2-097 | OBSERVATION | Gen 29:33 | Enabling conditions for reception (drawn from Q&A-031 and the anchor verse pattern): (1) Covenant participation: being within the relational structure that God's giving constitutes. The land-giving texts presuppose covenant membership as the reception condition. (2) Presented inner need: compassionate giving is triggered by visible inner suffering (Leah's condition, Gen 29:33) — the authentic expression of need enables responsive reception. (3) Posture of mourning/depletion: the eschatological giving is addressed to "those who mourn in Zion" (Isa 61:3) — the state of acknowledged need and depleted inner life. Blocking conditions: (1) Idolatrous misattribution — receiving the gift but attributing it to Baal (Hos 2:8, Q&A-032) blocks genuine reception even when the material gift arrives. (2) Covenant violation — faithlessness inverts giving-to into giving-over (Q&A-032), removing the receptive condition. (3) Refusal to give ear — Neh 9:30 — the rejection of prophetic warning closes the channel of Spirit-mediated reception. |
| OBS-060-T2-100 | OBSERVATION | Gen 29:33 | Primarily within covenantal contexts but with boundary-crossing capacity through mediation. The dominant mode (872-001) is explicitly covenantal. However, the compassionate giving (872-002) includes instances where the relational basis is need rather than formal covenant: Leah's condition (Gen 29:33) is within the covenant community but the giving is responsive to her individual inner suffering, not to her covenant membership per se. Isa 61:3 addresses "those who mourn in Zion" — the covenantal community, but the giving is to the condition of mourning, not to a specific covenant transaction. Isa 42:6 — "a covenant for the people, a light for the nations" — the servant mediates the giving beyond the covenant boundary. The characteristic operates primarily within covenant but is not constitutionally limited to it. |
| OBS-060-T2-101 | OBSERVATION | Gen 29:33 | The primary scope is the covenantal community — Abraham and his offspring (872-001 corpus), Israel and her sub-communities (Nehemiah, Hosea, Isaiah texts). Within this scope: individuals in need (Leah), the wilderness generation, the mourning in Zion, the depressed Servant. The judicial giving-over (872-004) includes Ephraim/Israel and the nations used as instruments of judgement, expanding the scope negatively. Excluded from covenantal giving: those outside the covenant relationship who have not received its basis (the nations receive the characteristic only through mediation — Isa 42:6). God's non-giving of glory to carved idols (Isa 42:8) establishes the limit at the divine level: idols are explicitly excluded from receiving divine glory-giving. The scope is defined by the relational structure: those in covenant receive covenantal giving; those outside receive at most mediated giving. |
| OBS-060-T2-110 | VERSE_PATTERN | Gen 29:33 | Yes — suffering is a pervasive context for the characteristic across three groups. (1) As the trigger for compassionate giving (872-002): Leah's suffering (being hated) triggers divine giving (Gen 29:33, OBS-060-037). Hosea's Israel suffering from lack, drought, and need is the context of giving in the broader 872-002 corpus. (2) As the context within which human self-giving is enacted (872-005): the Servant gives his back to those who strike — bodily suffering is the medium of the self-giving (Isa 50:6, OBS-060-045). Job's devastating losses are the context of his blessing-response (Job 1:21, OBS-060-044). (3) As the condition that eschatological giving addresses (872-007): "those who mourn in Zion" — mourning/grief is the before-state that the eschatological giving transforms (Isa 61:3, OBS-060-048). The characteristic operates as: response to suffering (compassionate mode), act within suffering (self-giving mode), and remedy for suffering (eschatological mode). |
| OBS-060-T2-114 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Isa 61:8 | Yes — group 872-007 is entirely eschatological in orientation and confirmed this at T0.2.3 (Q&A-006). Isa 61:3 names the eschatological endpoint: "oaks of righteousness, the planting of the Lord, that he may be glorified" — a stable, communal, identity-conferring state of righteousness that belongs to the age of divine restoration. Hos 2:15 invokes the Exodus as a type of the eschatological restoration — the future fullness is modelled on and exceeds the foundational covenant-giving moment. The present experience of covenantal giving (872-001) is itself oriented toward this fullness: the land given to Abraham is the earthly figuration of the eschatological inheritance. Isa 61:8 ("I will faithfully give them their recompense, and I will make an everlasting covenant with them") names the eschatological covenantal giving as the fullness toward which present covenantal giving points. |
| OBS-060-T2-115 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Isa 61:8 | The present experience of covenantal giving anticipates: (1) Completeness — every partial giving (land, provision, endowment) is oriented toward the fullness of the eschatological inheritance where the giving is total and permanent. The "everlasting covenant" and "everlasting name" of the Isaian texts name a giving that does not reserve or withhold. (2) Inner-being fullness — the eschatological giving transforms the inner person completely: faint spirit to praise, mourning to gladness, ashes to beauty. The present partial experience of inner renewal (Spirit-giving for instruction, compassionate provision for need) anticipates a state where no inner-being faculty remains in depletion. (3) Communal identity — "oaks of righteousness... the planting of the Lord" is communal: the present individual experiences of receiving divine giving anticipate a communal eschatological state of shared righteous identity. The present experience is partial, individual, and provisional; the future fullness is total, communal, and permanent. |
| OBS-060-T2-119 | VERSE_PATTERN | Gen 29:33 | Two sequential patterns are evidenced across the anchor verses. (1) Divine giving → human worship: Gen 12:7 (giving → altar-building), Hos 2:15 (giving → "she shall answer"), Isa 61:3 (giving → praise-garment). The characteristic consistently precedes worship/praise in these sequences. (2) Covenant faithfulness → covenant violation → judicial giving-over: the 872-001 → 872-004 sequence is a narrative pattern across the Neh 9, Hosea, and Jeremiah corpora. Faithfulness-as-giving (872-001) precedes faithlessness-response-giving (872-004) in the covenantal history. (3) Inner suffering → divine hearing → compassionate giving: Gen 29:33 shows this three-step sequence (Leah's suffering heard → child given). These are consistent enough across the corpus to constitute reliable sequential patterns. |
| OBS-060-T2-120 | VERSE_PATTERN | Gen 29:33 | The relationships are causal in all three patterns identified in Q&A-149. (1) Divine giving → worship: the giving causes the worship response — it would not occur without the prior giving. This is causal in the responsive direction. (2) Covenantal faithfulness → violation → judicial giving-over: the prior giving of covenant is the ground of the judicial accountability — the giving constitutes the relationship that makes violation possible and the giving-over its moral consequence. The causal chain runs from constitutive giving through violation to consequential giving. (3) Suffering → hearing → compassionate giving: the suffering is the causal trigger; divine hearing is the mediating perception; compassionate giving is the effect. The chain is causal throughout. None of the identified sequences are merely correlational — each has a directional causal logic grounded in the data. |
| OBS-060-T2-145 | VERSE_ANNOTATION | Gen 29:33 | The anchor verses are distributed across four contextual settings. (1) Covenantal: Gen 12:7, Gen 15:18, Mal 2:5, Neh 9:8 — formal covenant-establishment or covenantal renewal contexts. These settings require the giving to be read as covenantally binding, not merely generous. (2) Prophetic-judicial: Jer 12:7, Hos 13:11, Isa 42:8, Isa 47:6 — prophetic contexts of divine judgement and address to Israel. These require the giving to be read as morally consistent with the divine character, not arbitrary. (3) Eschatological-prophetic: Isa 61:3, Hos 2:15, Isa 35:2 — contexts of divine restoration announcement. These require the giving to be read as new-creation initiative, not mere restoration to prior state. (4) Narrative-individual: Gen 29:33, Job 1:21, Job 38:36 — individual persons encountering divine giving. These require attention to the specific relational situation of the individual. The diversity of settings confirms that inner-being giving is not a specialised sub-category of divine action but a pervasive mode present across the full range of biblical contexts. |
| OBS-060-T2-148 | OBSERVATION | Gen 29:33 | Two frameworks are relevant at different levels. (1) Moral philosophy (virtue ethics): the characteristic as analysed engages moral character (the primary dimension), voluntary action, the relationship between inner disposition and outer act, and the formation of stable character over time — all central concerns of virtue ethics (Aristotle, MacIntyre). Virtue ethics provides a framework for understanding how faithfulness-as-giving constitutes character rather than merely performing actions. (2) Attachment theory (developmental psychology/relational psychology): the responsive-giving mode (872-002) and the eschatological-restoration mode (872-007) engage attachment dynamics — attentiveness to the inner condition of the attached person, the protective withholding of harm (Hos 11:8), the restoration of relational responsiveness (Hos 2:15). Attachment theory illuminates the relational-dispositional dimension of the characteristic. Moral philosophy is the most useful for the overall characteristic; attachment theory is most useful for the compassionate-responsive mode. |

**SD pointers — direct (2)**

| Pointer | Priority | Strong's ref | Description |
|---|---|---|---|
| DIM-103-SD008 | MEDIUM | H8130 | Eccl 9:6 — love, hatred, and envy listed as the three constitutive inner orientations that cease at death. This triadic structure may define a fundamental taxonomy of relational inner states: love (toward/for), hatred (against), envy (desiring what another has). Does the Ecclesiastes triadic structure represent the OT's most explicit inner-being taxonomy? Cross-registry: love (103), hatred (75), envy registry. |
| DIM-103-SD024 | MEDIUM | H8130 | Gen 29:31 — 'when the Lord saw that Leah was hated, he opened her womb.' Hated/unloved state triggers divine compassion expressed through fertility. The womb as the site where divine love responds to human hatred. Cross-registry: love (103), hatred (75), grief (71). The unloved woman's womb being opened by God is one of the OT's most concentrated statements about divine love compensating for human lovelessness. |

### H8135 sin.ah — hating

**Identity & meaning**

1. Strong's: `H8135` · Lang: Hebrew · Owner: OWNER
2. Registry: R075 hatred · Legacy C-cluster: C07
3. Sub-group: `M06-A` (Hatred)
4. Term status: extracted · Evidential: — · Occurrences: 17

**Verses:** 16 distinct locations (see §2 for the verse table grouped by sub-group).

**Group memberships (3)**

| Group ID | Code | Description | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1201 | 902-001 | Term names hatred as an inner hostile disposition directed toward another person — a settled enmity that motivates action, can be concealed, and stands in direct contrast to love |  |
| 1202 | 902-002 | Term names hatred as an attributed inner disposition of God toward a people — projected or perceived divine enmity used to interpret suffering or covenant relationship |  |
| 1203 | 902-003 | Term names hatred as a fundamental inner human capacity — listed alongside love and envy as constitutive orientations of the person that define relational existence and cease at death |  |

**Findings — direct (Strong's mention) (0)**

(none)

**Findings — via anchor verse (5 unique)**

| Finding ID | Type | Matched anchor refs | Excerpt |
|---|---|---|---|
| OBS-103-T2-017 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Pro 10:12 | The structural opposite is hatred (sane — H8130, 139 active verses, OWNER term, OBS-103-030). Sane is embedded in R103 as an OWNER term — the programme treats hate as constitutive of the love vocabulary's boundary, not external to it. Lev 19:17 ('you shall not hate your brother in your heart') places hate as the inner alternative to love of neighbour (OBS-103-114). Pro 10:12 ('hatred stirs up strife, love covers all offences,' OBS-103-097) places them as causal-opposite forces with opposed social effects. The secondary structural opposite at the ultimate level is enmity with God: friendship with the world is enmity (echthra) with God (Jam 4:4, OBS-103-058). But hatred is the primary inner-being opposite — it is the same inner mechanism as love (directed orientation) running in the opposed direction. |
| OBS-103-T2-059 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Pro 10:12 | Yes — through the judgment of the love-object's worth and the assessment of love's hierarchy. Mat 10:37 (OBS-103-151) requires a judgment: 'whoever loves father or mother more than me is not worthy of me' — love operates through a comparative judgment of worth among competing objects. The ranking of loves (OBS-103-022 — love as four-mode structure) requires reason to navigate. Jam 4:4 (OBS-103-058): the reasoning that friendship with the world constitutes enmity with God is a logical judgment. Pro 10:12 (OBS-103-097): 'love covers all offences' — the judgment that covering is better than exposing is a reasoned moral assessment. Love requires and shapes the judgment-faculty at the level of determining what and whom to love, in what order, and how. |
| OBS-103-T2-065 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Pro 10:12 | Yes — love is the primary shaper of moral sensitivity in the data. Psa 97:10 (OBS-103-115): 'O you who love the Lord, hate evil' — love of God directly produces moral sensitivity to evil (the capacity to hate what is wrong). Lev 19:17 (OBS-103-114): the prohibition on hating the brother in the heart implies that moral sensitivity recognises inner hate as morally significant. 1Cor 13:6 (within OBS-103-127): love 'does not rejoice in wrongdoing' — love shapes the moral sensitivity that recognises wrongdoing as something not to be celebrated. Pro 10:12 (OBS-103-097): love's moral sensitivity distinguishes between hatred-that-stirs-strife and love-that-covers — the faculty that makes this distinction is morally sensitised by love. Love functions as the moral-sensitivity calibrator: it determines what the inner person registers as morally significant and how they register it. |
| OBS-103-T2-113 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Pro 10:12 | Yes — embedded as OWNER. H8130 sane (to hate, 139 active / 156 total) is the structural opposite within the registry (OBS-103-030). H8131 sena (hating, 1 active) is a second form. The hate vocabulary is not XREF but OWNER — the programme treats the structural opposite as constituent of the love vocabulary's boundary (OBS-103-019). Additionally: the philo-compound negative forms (afilarguros — not-money-loving; pseudadelfos — false-brother) name the absence of specific love-forms. The disordered love vocabulary names love's distorted presence rather than its absence. True lovelessness (absence without misdirection) is not prominently named — the data suggests the inner mechanism is always present and always directed at something; the question is always the object, not the presence or absence of love-capacity. |
| OBS-103-T2-135 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | Pro 10:12 | Yes — and the data makes this explicit. Psa 97:10 (OBS-103-115): 'O you who love the Lord, hate evil' — hatred of evil is commanded of those who love God. Righteous hatred is not love's failure but love's necessary complement: you cannot love God and be indifferent to what opposes him. Lev 19:17 (OBS-103-114): 'you shall not hate your brother in your heart' — hatred of the brother is wrong. The same inner-being mechanism (hatred as directed-aversion) can be rightly directed (at evil) or wrongly directed (at the brother). This is the precise structural parallel to love: love rightly directed (toward God and neighbour) vs love wrongly directed (toward money, pleasure, world). Hatred operates under the same moral logic as love: the mechanism is morally neutral; the object determines the moral quality. The ordered inner life requires both rightly directed love AND rightly directed hatred. |

**SD pointers — direct (0)**

(none)

**Auxiliary data**

_Root family (1):_

1. `SANI` (Hebrew): hated

_Related words (6):_

1. H8130 sa.ne → to hate
2. H8146 sa.ni → hated
3. H8149 se.nir → Senir
4. H8130 sa.ne → to hate
5. H8146 sa.ni → hated
6. H8149 se.nir → Senir

**Findings — via anchor verse (5 unique)**

| Finding ID | Type | Matched anchor refs | Excerpt |
|---|---|---|---|
| OBS-103-T2-067 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | 2Ti 3:3 | This is one of love's most significant contributions in the data. Belovedness as identity: agapētos (OBS-103-040, OBS-103-122) — the believer's primary identity designation is 'loved by God and called.' Being loved constitutes who the person is; identity is received through the love-relationship, not self-generated. Mat 3:17 (OBS-103-120): the Father's declaration 'this is my beloved Son' constitutes Christ's identity — being named beloved is identity-conferral. Joh 13:35 (OBS-103-129): the community's identity ('my disciples') is constituted by its love for one another — what you love constitutes your community identity. What you love as the individual also constitutes personal identity: the money-lover (OBS-103-132), the God-lover (OBS-103-118), the world-lover (OBS-103-148) — love is the diagnostic identity-marker. Identity in the biblical data is constituted by: (a) being loved (passive — agapētos) and (b) what you love (active — the love-object as identity-definer). |
| OBS-103-T2-114 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | 2Ti 3:3 | Yes — two primary person-type terms: (a) **H2623 chasid** (pious/godly one, 33 active) — the person-type of chesed. The chasid is defined by their inner character of covenantal love toward God (OBS-103-026). (b) **G5384 filos** (friend, 27 active) — the person-type of phileō. The filos is one whose inner orientation of loyal affection has become their defining relational identity (OBS-103-018). Additional person-type compounds: filagathos (lover of good — positive), filarguros (money-lover — negative), filotheos (God-lover), filēdonos (pleasure-lover), filautos (self-lover — via 2Ti 3:2). The philo-compound system generates person-types for each form of love (OBS-103-017). The programme has the richest person-type vocabulary in the programme for any single characteristic — the love-vocabulary directly generates who you are from what you love. |
| OBS-103-T2-128 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | 2Ti 3:3 | Yes — love is always directed. The grammar confirms this: agapaō always takes a direct object; the philo-compound system is entirely object-defining (love-of-X where X determines the compound). No instance of undirected love appears in the data — love is constitutively directional (OBS-103-017, OBS-103-009). The object determines love's moral character entirely: the inner mechanism is identical whether the object is God (filotheos — morally ordered) or pleasure (filēdonos — morally disordered) or money (filarguros). This is the data's most consistently evidenced structural feature: the same inner act of attachment produces radically different moral outcomes based solely on the object. The moral life in the biblical data is substantially a question of love's direction — not whether one loves but what one loves. This confirms L-004's anticipated finding (below). |
| OBS-103-T2-129 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | 2Ti 3:3 | Yes — this is one of the data's most strongly evidenced structural claims. 2Ti 3:2-4 (OBS-103-137) lists philautos (self-lover) and philēdonos (pleasure-lover) vs filotheos (God-lover) as the diagnostic markers distinguishing the last-days person from the faithful person. Joh 3:19 (OBS-103-147): 'people loved the darkness' — the love-choice is the diagnostic of judgment. Joh 13:35 (OBS-103-129): 'by this all will know that you are my disciples, if you have love for one another' — the community's love-practice is the external diagnostic of their identity. Mat 10:37 (OBS-103-151): whoever loves father or mother more than Christ 'is not worthy of me' — the hierarchy of love is the diagnostic of worthiness. What a person loves is not merely a preference — it is a revelation of what they are. The love-diagnostic is both internal (self-knowledge) and external (publicly legible community identity). |
| OBS-103-T2-131 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | 2Ti 3:3 | Yes — the philo-compound disordered forms constitute a taxonomy (OBS-103-036, OBS-103-017): filarguria/filarguros (love of money — 3 groups), filēdonos (love of pleasure), filoneikia/filoneikos (love of dispute), filoprōteuō (love of being first), filia tou kosmou (friendship with world — Jam 4:4), agapaō-darkness/world (Joh 3:19, 2Ti 4:10), agavah (lust — H5691), filautos (love of self — 2Ti 3:2). The structural logic organising the taxonomy: all disordered loves are the same inner mechanism (directed attachment) applied to one of three wrong object-classes: (a) **Material objects** — money, pleasure; (b) **Social-positional objects** — primacy, dispute-victory; (c) **The self** — self-love, friendship with the world as self-assertion. The taxonomy is not arbitrary — it maps the full range of objects that compete with God and the neighbour as the proper objects of love. The disordered loves are a systematic counter-ordering of the inner person's relational architecture. |

## §4. Appendix — items linked at registry or collection level

### §4.1 Findings from contributor registries with no term-level link (188)

These findings sit on a registry that contributes terms to this cluster, but their text and anchor verses don't resolve to any specific cluster term. Candidates for term-level enrichment.

| Finding ID | Type | Registry | Anchor verses | Excerpt |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| DIM-001-001 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | R001 abomination |  | The new covenant transformation group (3272-001: diatithēmi — the covenantal act writing divine law on the inner mind and heart) appears in the abomination registry. This places the new covenant's inner transformation as the divine answer to abomination and inner defilement. Session B should examine whether the abomination cluster's verse evidence shows the new covenant specifically as the remedy for abomination — and whether this pattern recurs across the cluster. |
| DIM-65-001 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | R065 generosity |  | agathos (G0018) groups in Reg 65 frame the inner being's relationship to goodness in four registers: (1) goodness as character source (good heart — Character/Disposition, 881-002), (2) goodness as moral command (do good — Moral/Conscience, 881-003), (3) goodness as inner conflict (want but cannot — Volitional/Will, 881-005), (4) goodness as divine attribute (only God is good — Theological/Divine-Human, 881-001). Group 881-005 is analytically most significant — the gap between inner desire for good and capacity to perform it is the heart of Pauline anthropology. Session B should examine how these four registers of goodness interact and what they reveal about the inner being's relationship to moral reality. |
| DIM-98-001 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | R098 justice |  | H4941G mish.pat (Reg 98) and H4941H mish.pat (Reg 24) are the same Hebrew term across two registries: five groups in Reg 98 and three groups in Reg 24 constitute the full inner-being profile. Session B must read both registries' mish.pat groups together for a complete analysis. |

This is one of the most analytically significant tensions in the programme. Session B must examine this carefully. |

This fourfold pattern in a single Hebrew root is a major Session B analytical focus. |
