Session B should map the vocabulary of anger-governance as a structured inner-being claim about will, character, and spiritual posture. |
| DIM-4-002 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | R004 anger |  | Two groups (1552-001: fierce anger co-existing with grief/loyalty; 37-003: righteous anger co-existing with sorrow at hardness of heart) show the inner being holding anger and love, or anger and grief, simultaneously as genuine compound affective states. Session B should examine whether Scripture treats compound anger-with-grief as a distinct inner-being mode and what theological conditions produce it. |
| DIM-103-001 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | R103 love |  | The love registry spans the broadest relational vocabulary in the programme — agapē, phileō, chesed, and related terms — encompassing God's love for humanity (GOD dominant), human love toward God, mutual love among persons, and disordered love. Session B should map the full spectrum of love's inner-being architecture: what distinguishes the different forms, how they interrelate, and what the coexistence of eros/philia/agapē in the same registry reveals about the inner-being's capacity for love. |
| DIM-103-002 | DIMENSION_REVIEW | R103 love |  | Group 535-001 (ye.di.dut — beloved of Gods soul, Reg 103) is anchored by Jer 12:7: I have given the beloved of my soul into the hands of her enemies. The phrase ye.di.dut nap.shi (beloved of my soul/nephesh) attributes an intimate inner-being category to God — God has a nephesh, and the beloved relationship is located there. This raises a significant inner-being question for Session B of Reg 103: does the love vocabulary of Reg 103 contain a sub-pattern of terms that attribute inner-being states to God with the same vocabulary used for human inner-being states? The terms ye.di.dut (beloved of my soul), ra.cha.mim (my heart yearns — Jer 31:20 in group 551-001), and the dod vocabulary (God as lover/beloved in Song and prophets) may all encode a divine inner-being reality using the same vocabulary as the human inner person. Session B should investigate whether Reg 103 contains a theological claim about divine inner-being experience, and how this connects to the programmes governing question about the inner characteristics of the human person. |
| OBS-103-T2-001 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Exo 34:6, Jer 31:3, Song 8:6, 1Jo 4:8 (via flag), Mat 3:17 | The verse evidence reveals that love is not merely an attribute God exercises but a characterisation of what God is. The divine self-declaration formula at Exo 34:6 (OBS-103-069) names rachum (compassionate) + chesed (steadfast love) as the first two inner attributes God proclaims of himself — love leads the divine self-portrait. Jer 31:3 names God's love as 'everlasting' (ahavat olam) — a qualifier that exceeds any human love-form (OBS-103-093). Song 8:6 names love's flame as 'the very flame of the Lord' (shalhevetyah) — grounding love's intensity in the divine nature itself (OBS-103-096). The data culminates in the NT claim (1Jo 4:8 — God is love), carried in the registry as PH2-103-004 and evidenced structurally by the entire divine love vocabulary across the data. The characteristic being imaged in the human person is therefore not a quality God has alongside others but God's own constitutive being-as-love. |
| OBS-103-T2-002 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Jer 12:7, Jer 31:20, Exo 34:6, Joh 3:16, 1Jo 4:19 | Scripture attributes love to God across both testaments and with unprecedented density in R103 — 14+ GOD-dominant groups (OBS-103-034). The attribution operates at three levels: (a) love as God's relational disposition toward persons (chesed-GOD group 536-001; agapaō-GOD group 571-002; rachamim-GOD group 544-001); (b) love as God's inner-being experience — God's soul has a beloved (Jer 12:7, OBS-103-086), God's inner organs move with compassion (Jer 31:20, Isa 63:15, OBS-103-106, OBS-103-117), God grieves the withdrawal of his love; (c) love as what God is ontologically (1Jo 4:8 — held via PH2-103-004). The significance for the human person: because love is constitutive of God's being, it is the primary characteristic through which the human person bears the divine image. A human person who loves is not merely imitating a divine behaviour but reflecting the divine nature. The love-capacity is the image-capacity. |
| OBS-103-T2-003 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Mat 22:37, Lev 19:18, Joh 13:34, 1Jo 4:19 | The verse evidence points to love as the characteristic that equips the human person to participate in the relational structure of divine life — to enter and sustain the three directional axes identified in OBS-103-035 (vertical-descending, vertical-ascending, horizontal). Love of God with all heart, soul, and mind (Mat 22:37, OBS-103-139) equips the person to respond to the divine love that constitutes them. Love of neighbour (Lev 19:18, OBS-103-071) equips the person to bear the image of God toward other persons. Love in community (Joh 13:34, OBS-103-145) equips the person to live within the relational structure that constitutes the community of God's people. Together: love equips the person to be the image-bearer — to reflect God's own love outward in every relational direction. The great commandment (love God, love neighbour) implies that love is the purpose-function of the human person as created: the person is made to love, and love is what the person most fundamentally is for. |
| OBS-103-T2-004 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Song 2:16, Exo 34:6, Mat 5:44, Luk 7:47 | The evidence strongly implies love is part of original created design — the great commandment assumes love as the constitutive purpose of the human person, not as a remedial response. Song of Songs presents love (ahavah, dod) in a creation-delight context without reference to sin or fall — erotic love as given, not remedial. The divine self-declaration (Exo 34:6) attributes love to God prior to and independent of the fall. However, the data also shows love operating distinctively in response to the fallen condition: agapē of enemies (Mat 5:44, OBS-103-143) presupposes enemies exist; racham/compassion (OBS-103-029) responds to suffering that is post-fall in character; forgiveness-love (Luk 7:47, OBS-103-020 via SD pointer) presupposes guilt. The data does not contain an explicit statement that love existed in creation before the fall — the gap in pre-fall love evidence is noted. Both dimensions appear present but the evidence is stronger for love as created design than as purely remedial response. |
| OBS-103-T2-005 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Jer 31:34, Psa 27:13, 1Th 3:12, Song 8:6 | Yes, and clearly. Jer 31:34 (OBS-103-072) presents the new covenant as the eschatological fulfilment of love's neighbour-mediated form — in the final state, neighbour-teaching of God-knowledge is superseded by direct divine knowledge. The new covenant is love's eschatological completion, not its abolition. Psa 27:13 (OBS-103-080) — 'I shall look upon the goodness of the Lord in the land of the living' — names future vision of God's love/goodness as the orientation of hope. 1Th 3:12 (OBS-103-130) — 'may the Lord make you increase and abound in love' — treats love as a growing reality, moving toward greater fullness. 1Jo 4:18 (via SP-103-029) implies that perfect love casts out fear — 'perfect love' is an eschatological state toward which current love moves. The trajectory is from love-as-now to love-as-perfected: love is eschatologically oriented. |
| OBS-103-T2-006 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | 1Jo 4:19, Joh 13:34, Rom 8:29, Gal 2:20 | Love expresses the divine image in the human person through structural mirroring: the same relational orientations attributed to God (love toward persons, compassion toward the suffering, faithful loyalty within bonds) are commanded of and available to the human person. The mirroring is not analogical but participatory in the data: 1Jo 4:19 ('we love because he first loved us') presents human love as flowing from and enabled by divine love — the same love, not merely an imitation. Rom 8:29 (OBS-103-076) — predestination to conformity with the image of the Son — makes love-conformity the goal of the divine image-restoration project. Joh 13:34 ('as I have loved you, so you must love one another') makes the divine love the model and measure of the human love that bears the image. The aspect of likeness instantiated: love as relational-orientation-toward-persons is the primary mode in which the human person resembles and participates in the divine being. |
| OBS-103-T2-007 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Jer 12:7, Jer 31:20, 1Jo 4:19, Exo 34:6, Joh 13:34 | The evidence strongly suggests love is shared, not merely analogical. The vocabulary is explicitly common: God's nephesh has a beloved using the same term as the human person's beloved (OBS-103-086); God's inner organs (me'eka) are moved using somatic vocabulary parallel to the human compassion-response (OBS-103-106, OBS-103-117); agapē is the term both for God's love toward persons and the commanded love of person toward God and others. The LXX use of agapē to translate chesed bridges the Testaments — the same vocabulary governs both divine and human love. DIM-103-002 (§N item) is precisely this question and is confirmed: the love vocabulary of R103 consistently attributes inner-being states to God with the same vocabulary used for human inner-being. This is not analogy but shared characteristic — love is the one characteristic in the programme where divine and human possession is most evidentially co-extensive. |
| OBS-103-T2-008 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Joh 13:35, Mat 5:44-45, 1Jo 4:8 (via flag) | The data provides an unusually direct answer. Joh 13:35 (OBS-103-129) — 'by this all people will know that you are my disciples, if you have love for one another' — makes love the externally legible mark of the divine image in the community. 1Jo 4:8 (via flag) — 'whoever does not love does not know God, for God is love' — states that lovelessness constitutes non-knowledge of God. The absence of love is not merely a moral deficiency; it is an epistemic and ontological condition: the person who does not love does not know God and therefore does not bear the divine image in its proper operation. Conversely, the presence of love — particularly love of enemies (Mat 5:44-45, OBS-103-144) — constitutes identity as a son/daughter of God. Love is thus the diagnostic marker of the divine image's condition: present and active = image bearing; absent or disordered = image distorted. |
| OBS-103-T2-009 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Eze 16:8, Mat 3:17, Luk 15:20, Isa 5:1 | Yes — extensively. The dod vocabulary of the Song is the most concentrated typological deployment: human eros/marital love functions as the vehicle for God's love for Israel (Isa 5:1 OBS-103-083; Eze 16:8 OBS-103-083b) and in the prophetic-allegorical tradition as the figure of divine-human covenantal love. God's love for Israel is called 'the time of love' (Eze 16:8) using marital vocabulary. The father-son love (Mat 3:17, OBS-103-120) functions typologically: the Father's love for the Son at baptism is simultaneously the origin-point from which all love flows (SD-016) and the pattern of divine-to-human love in redemption. The parable of the prodigal son (Luk 15:20, OBS-103-057) deploys parental love typologically — the father's running, embracing, and kissing figure God's reception of the returning sinner. Typological use runs in both directions (OT human love → divine love type; NT divine love → human love pattern). |
| OBS-103-T2-010 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Joh 13:34, 1Jo 4:19, Eze 16:8, Jer 31:3 | The evidence shows both directions operating but with a clear asymmetry. In the OT prophetic tradition: human marital/parental love → divine covenantal love (the human type points toward and is fulfilled in the divine). In the NT: divine love → human love (the divine instance establishes the pattern for the human: 'as I have loved you' — Joh 13:34; 'we love because he first loved us' — 1Jo 4:19). The asymmetry is that in the NT the direction inverts: the human type has served its purpose; the divine original now directly constitutes the human instance. The love-structure of the inner being therefore participates in a typological movement across the canon: created human love → figures divine love → divine love in Christ becomes the source and standard of human love in the new covenant. |
| OBS-103-T2-011 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Mat 22:37, Lev 19:18 | The characteristic is called 'love' — a name that in English collapses a vocabulary of multiple Hebrew and Greek terms into a single referent. The name signals an orientation outward: love is always toward something or someone; it cannot be self-contained. Even the word's grammar in Scripture consistently requires a direct object (love of God, love of neighbour, love of enemy, love of money). The name also signals relational constitution: the one who loves is partly constituted by who and what they love. The programme's description note ('most foundational and most theologically dense word in the entire corpus,' OBS-103-004) signals that the name functions as an organising category for the entire inner-being vocabulary. |
| OBS-103-T2-012 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Psa 63:3, Joh 13:34, Isa 49:15 | At the definitional level, the primary terms reveal a structured vocabulary rather than a single concept. Hebrew: chesed (covenant-faithfulness, binding loyalty), ahavah (intense personal love including eros), racham/rachamim (compassion — love responding to suffering), dod (beloved, erotic love of the Song). Greek: agapē (willed self-giving love, LXX/NT coinage), phileō (natural affection), philia compounds (love directed toward a specified object). The terms do not all name the same inner state at different intensities — they name structurally distinct modes of love's operation. Chesed is obligatory-covenantal; agapē is volitional-unconditional; phileō is naturally affective; racham is compassion-responsive. At the definitional level, 'love' in this registry is not one thing but a family of related inner orientations sharing the common structure of directed-attachment-to-an-other (OBS-103-033). |
| OBS-103-T2-013 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Mat 22:37, Jam 4:4, 1Jo 4:19 | All three. Directional: love always has a direction — toward God, toward neighbour, toward the beloved, or toward disordered objects (money, pleasure, world). The moral question of love is always the question of its direction (OBS-103-017). Relational: love cannot exist in isolation — it is constitutively relational, requiring at minimum a lover and a beloved. The relational structure is not incidental but essential (OBS-103-035). Constitutional: love operates at the deepest level of the inner person — the great commandment (Mat 22:37) requires 'all your heart and soul and mind,' indicating that love engages the entire constitutional depth of the inner being (OBS-103-139). The enquiry is oriented from the outset toward a characteristic that is simultaneously moral (choice of direction), relational (requires another), and constitutional (engages the whole person). |
| OBS-103-T2-014 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Mat 22:37, Psa 63:3, Rom 1:7, 1Jo 4:19 | Love in the data is simultaneously a disposition (stable inner orientation toward), an act (commanded, exercised, expressed — agapaō is consistently verbal), and a condition (one who is loved — agapētos — is in a constitutive relational state). It is not primarily an emotion, though it produces emotional states (joy, grief, rest). The commanded form (Mat 22:37 — 'you shall love') establishes love as an act of the will, not purely a felt state. The dispositional form (chesed as God's defining attribute, OBS-103-025) establishes love as a stable character quality. The received form (agapētos as identity, OBS-103-040) establishes love as a constitutive condition the person exists within. Love is therefore tripartite: disposition + act + condition — inner orientation that produces acts and exists within a condition of being-loved. This is the most structurally complex inner-being phenomenon in the programme. |
| OBS-103-T2-015 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Mat 22:37, 1Cor 13:4, Gal 5:22 | Structurally complex from the first encounter. The four-mode taxonomy (OBS-103-033) — willed covenantal, compassionate responsive, relational-social, intense erotic — is the first-level complexity. Beneath that, the common structure: directed attachment toward an object, whose moral quality is entirely determined by the object (OBS-103-009, OBS-103-017). The disordered forms (OBS-103-036) share the same structure as the righteous forms. The three-axis directional structure (OBS-103-035) adds spatial complexity: love operates in three directions simultaneously. The tripartite kind (Q&A-016) adds ontological complexity: disposition, act, and condition. Love appears to be the programme's most structurally composite inner-being characteristic — not simple but architecturally layered. |
| OBS-103-T2-016 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Mat 22:37, 1Jo 4:19, Joh 13:35, Gal 5:22 | Working description: Love is the primary inner-being orientation of the human person — the directed attachment of the whole inner self toward God, persons, and the good, operating as both the deepest constitutional disposition and the foundational act of the will, producing and sustaining all relational bonds. It locates principally at the heart-soul interface (Spirit-Soul classification confirmed). It engages the will (commanded), the cognition (requires knowledge of the beloved), the emotion (produces joy, grief, rest depending on the beloved's presence/absence), and the body (expressed somatically in kiss, embrace, tears). Its impact: it constitutes the person's relational identity (who you love defines who you are), organises all other inner-being characteristics (love of God requires hatred of evil; love of God produces fruit), and is the externally legible mark of the community's identity (Joh 13:35). Its absence is the diagnostic indicator of the divine image's distortion (1Jo 4:8). |
| OBS-103-T2-019 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Mat 5:44, Lev 19:18, Hos 6:6 | What love is not, from the data: love is not sentiment — it is commanded (Mat 22:37) and exercised irrespective of feeling (enemy-love, Mat 5:44). Love is not mere natural affection — phileō is insufficient as the full standard; agapē and chesed exceed phileō in obligatory reach. Love is not the same as desire (R043) — the desire registry owns the primary ahav verbal form (H0157G); desire and love share a mechanism but the programme treats them as distinct (OBS-103-010, OBS-103-022). Love is not the same as goodness (R067) — the tov family is XREF; love produces goodness but is not identical with it (OBS-103-014). The precise boundary between love and compassion (R023), kindness (R099), and mercy (R111) cannot be fully drawn from Stage 2a evidence alone — these are the programme's adjacent characteristics whose distinctions require dedicated treatment in Session D. Partial: the internal boundary is evidenced; the inter-registry distinctions are named as gaps deferred to Session D. |
| OBS-103-T2-020 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Lam 3:22, Isa 49:15, Mat 5:44, Joh 11:36 | Four primary modes of operation, each evidenced across the anchor verse corpus: (1) **Covenantal-dispositional mode** (chesed, agapē): Love as stable inner orientation of faithful loyalty — not feeling-contingent, not revocable by the beloved's failure. God's chesed 'never ceases' (Lam 3:22, OBS-103-088); human chesed is written on the heart as character (Pro 3:3, OBS-103-090). This mode operates at the level of character — the deep stable orientation. (2) **Compassionate-responsive mode** (racham, splanchnizō): Love that is activated by the beloved's suffering — the inner-organ movement (OBS-103-105, OBS-103-116). This mode responds to need; it is not passive but activated. (3) **Volitional-costly mode** (agapē — enemy-love, self-giving): Love that operates against the inner grain of natural preference. Mat 5:44 (OBS-103-143), Joh 15:13 (OBS-103-125). This mode requires the will's deliberate engagement to exceed what natural affection would produce. (4) **Affective-relational mode** (phileō, ahavah-intense, dod): Love as naturally felt warm attachment — the affection for friends, the longing for the beloved. This mode is experienced; it is love in its felt dimension. The four modes are not always distinguishable in a single verse but are analytically distinct operations of the same inner orientation. |
| OBS-103-T2-021 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Mat 22:37, Mat 5:44, Song 2:16, Pro 3:3 | Yes — context and direction both shape the mode. Direction: love toward God operates in the volitional-dispositional mode most prominently (commanded; requires the whole person — Mat 22:37, OBS-103-139); love toward the neighbour operates in both the dispositional and the costly-volitional modes; love toward the beloved (marital/erotic) operates in the affective-intense mode (dod, ahavah — Song vocabulary, OBS-103-041); love toward the enemy operates exclusively in the costly-volitional mode (OBS-103-143). Constitutional level: at the spirit/soul boundary (sb_classification confirmed), love appears to have its deepest location at the spirit level (the willed, faithful chesed) and its experiential expression at the soul level (the felt ahavah/phileō). At the heart level (OBS-103-126) love is infused by the Spirit and inscribed as character. The constitutional level shapes how love presents: deep-spirit love is more chesed-like; soul-surface love is more phileō-like. |
| OBS-103-T2-023 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | 1Jo 4:19, Zep 3:17, Psa 127:2, Joh 11:36 | The data evidences three immediate response patterns, each associated with a primary love-encounter type: (1) **Responsive love** — 1Jo 4:19: the immediate response to receiving divine love is love in return. Love received generates love given — the response is the same characteristic activated in the receiver. (2) **Rest/stillness** — Zep 3:17 (OBS-103-094): God's love toward Israel produces quieting — the immediate inner response to the experience of being loved is rest, not striving. Psa 127:2 (OBS-103-084): being-beloved produces effortless sleep (rest as divine love-gift). (3) **Grief as love-evidence** — Joh 11:36 (OBS-103-149), 2Sa 1:26 (OBS-103-095), Joh 21:17 (OBS-103-153): the immediate response to love's loss or to love's cost is grief — the inner collapse or distress that reveals the depth of the prior love. This is not a response to love per se but to love's absence or cost, and it is consistently love's most visible immediate evidence. |
| OBS-103-T2-024 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | 1Jo 4:19, Zep 3:17, Song 5:6, Luk 15:20 | The response varies by the type of love-encounter. When divine love is received: the immediate response is love-in-return (1Jo 4:19) or rest (Zep 3:17, Psa 127:2). When love is expressed at cost (forgiveness-love, enemy-love): the immediate response in the giver is not named directly. When love is lost: the immediate response is grief (Song 5:6, OBS-103-062; 2Sa 1:26, OBS-103-095). When the beloved is encountered: the immediate response is delight and longing (Song 2:16, OBS-103-061; Luk 15:20 — the father's compassion-movement at sight of the returning son, OBS-103-057). The variation is systematic, not random: the type of encounter determines the response type. There is no single invariant immediate response to love — the response depends on the direction of the encounter (giving vs receiving vs losing vs encountering). |
| OBS-103-T2-025 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Pro 3:3, 1Pe 1:22, Psa 16:11, 1Th 3:12, Joh 14:15 | The verse evidence identifies several sustained effects of love in the inner being: (1) **Character formation** — Pro 3:3 (OBS-103-090): chesed written on the heart over time becomes character. 1Pe 1:22 (OBS-103-124): purified souls move toward sincere brotherly love — love as the goal of sustained inner formation. (2) **Joy and fullness** — Psa 16:11 (OBS-103-112): in God's presence (sustained love-relationship) there is fullness of joy and pleasures forevermore. The sustained love-relationship with God produces an abiding experiential fullness. (3) **Growth** — 1Th 3:12 (OBS-103-130): love can increase and abound over time. Love is not static but grows under the Lord's enabling. (4) **Community cohesion** — Joh 13:35 (OBS-103-129): sustained mutual love becomes the externally legible identity of the community — a sustained social effect rather than a momentary one. (5) **Obedience pattern** — Joh 14:15 (OBS-103-140): sustained love of Christ produces a sustained pattern of commandment-keeping. The inner orientation produces an enduring behavioural pattern. |
| OBS-103-T2-026 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Joh 13:35, Rom 1:7, Joh 14:15, Jer 31:14 | From the data: sustained possession of love establishes — (a) **identity as beloved** (agapētos — the one constituted by divine love, OBS-103-040, OBS-103-122): sustained divine love toward the person establishes the identity of being-loved; (b) **relational capacity** — sustained love of neighbour establishes the inner orientation of fairness, care, and honesty that Lev 19 describes (OBS-103-071); (c) **community legibility** — the community constituted by mutual love becomes publicly readable (Joh 13:35, OBS-103-129); (d) **faith-pattern** — sustained love of God produces sustained commandment-keeping (Joh 14:15, OBS-103-140); (e) **soul-satisfaction** — sustained experience of God's goodness/love satisfies the soul's deepest hunger (Jer 31:14, OBS-103-081). The overarching capacity established: the person becomes capable of giving what they have received — sustained reception of divine love equips the person to love others. |
| OBS-103-T2-027 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Zep 3:17, Pro 3:3, Joh 13:35, Jer 31:14 | Yes — the distinction is clear. The immediate response to love is primarily experiential: rest/stillness (Zep 3:17), responsive love (1Jo 4:19), or grief (Song 5:6). The sustained effect is primarily constitutional and communal: character formation (Pro 3:3), identity-establishment (agapētos), community legibility (Joh 13:35), and soul-satisfaction (Jer 31:14). The immediate response is felt; the sustained effect is what the person becomes and what the community is constituted as. This distinction maps onto the programme's spirit-soul boundary: the immediate response operates at the soul-affective level; the sustained effect operates at the spirit-character level and the relational-community level. |
| OBS-103-T2-028 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | 1Pe 1:22, Jam 2:23, Joh 3:19, Luk 15:20 | From the data: (a) **obedience** — 1Pe 1:22 (OBS-103-124): soul-purification through obedience enables sincere love. The purified soul is the condition for authentic love. (b) **faith** — Jam 2:23 (OBS-103-053): Abraham's faith is what constitutes him as 'friend of God.' Faith as the inner condition through which love-relationship with God becomes possible. (c) **openness / not loving the darkness** — Joh 3:19 (OBS-103-147): those who love darkness cannot receive the light. The inner orientation away from evil is the negative condition for receiving love. (d) **being the returning prodigal** — Luk 15:20 (OBS-103-057): the son's return (movement toward the father) is the condition for the father's embrace. Some movement toward the source of love appears to be a condition for its reception. Gap: the data does not contain an explicit systematic account of reception-conditions. The conditions above are inferred from contexts where love is given and received. The gap is noted. |
| OBS-103-T2-029 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Joh 3:19, 1Ti 6:10, 1Cor 13:4-7, Gal 2:4 | The data names several inner blockers: (a) **love of darkness** — Joh 3:19 (OBS-103-147): the inner orientation toward darkness is the condition that prevents reception of love-as-light. The person who loves the darkness does not receive the light; the blocker is the prior love-commitment to a wrong object. (b) **love of money** — 1Ti 6:10 (OBS-103-132): love of money causes departure from faith — the love of a wrong object displaces the reception of divine love. (c) **pride/self-seeking** — 1Cor 13:4-7 (OBS-103-127): love of self expressed as arrogance and self-seeking is explicitly named as what love is not — the self-orientation blocks the other-orientation that genuine love requires. (d) **false-brotherhood orientation** — Gal 2:4 (OBS-103-068): the concealed inner agenda of the false brother prevents genuine love-reception within the community. The pattern: all inner blockers are disordered loves — prior commitments to wrong objects that displace the capacity for rightly directed love. |
| OBS-103-T2-030 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Joh 3:19, Luk 16:14, 2Ti 4:10 | The data provides several instances: (a) Joh 3:19 (OBS-103-147) — the person who encounters light-as-love and does not receive it 'loved the darkness' — the inner state is commitment to the alternative; the non-reception is an inner-being act of love misdirected. (b) Luk 16:14 (OBS-103-136) — the Pharisees who were money-lovers ridiculed Jesus' teaching; their inner state is intellectual rejection grounded in love-of-money. (c) 2Ti 4:10 (OBS-103-148) — Demas, in love with the present world, deserts: the non-reception of love-community is an act of love toward the world instead. The pattern is consistent: the person who does not receive love is not loveless — they are loving the wrong thing. Lovelessness in the sense of having no love-capacity does not appear in the data; what appears is love misdirected. |
| OBS-103-T2-031 | OBSERVATION | R103 love | Mat 22:37, 1Jo 4:19, Joh 13:34 | Primary dimension: **Relational Disposition**. This is the confirmed Dimension Review result (v1.9, 2026-04-09) and is well-supported by the data. Love is fundamentally orientation-toward-another — the directed attachment of the inner person toward an object. The relational structure is constitutive, not incidental: love cannot exist without a direction and an object (OBS-103-015, OBS-103-035). The Dimension Review classification is confirmed as well-grounded by the full anchor verse reading in Stage 2a. |
| OBS-103-T2-032 | OBSERVATION | R103 love | Mat 22:37, Lev 19:18, 1Jo 4:19, Joh 13:35 | The Relational Disposition classification is supported by: (a) the consistent directional structure of the vocabulary — love always has an object toward which it is oriented (OBS-103-017); (b) the three-axis relational architecture (GOD → HUMAN, HUMAN → GOD, HUMAN → HUMAN, OBS-103-035); (c) the 14+ GOD-dominant groups naming divine love as relational orientation (OBS-103-034); (d) the person-type terms (filos, chasid, agapētos) that name the relational identity constituted by love (OBS-103-018, OBS-103-026, OBS-103-040); (e) the group descriptions which consistently describe love as 'inner orientation toward' or 'relational disposition' in their language. |
| OBS-103-T2-033 | OBSERVATION | R103 love | Pro 3:3, Joh 11:36, Mat 5:44, Mat 10:37 | Secondary dimensions evidenced: (a) **Moral Character** — chesed written on the heart (Pro 3:3, OBS-103-090), chasid as the person of covenant-character (OBS-103-026), love-of-good (filagathos) as a character disposition (OBS-103-134). Love as stable character (not just act) carries Moral Character alongside Relational Disposition. (b) **Emotion-Positive** — the affective-relational modes (phileō, ahavah-intense, dod) carry positive emotional content: delight, joy, longing (OBS-103-061, OBS-103-112). (c) **Volition** — enemy-love (Mat 5:44) and the ranking of loves (Mat 10:37) are explicitly volitional — choices against natural preference. These secondary dimensions do not compete with Relational Disposition; they describe the faculties through which love's relational orientation is expressed. The primary dimension correctly captures the constitutive structure; the secondary dimensions capture the modes. |
| OBS-103-T2-034 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Gal 5:22, Rom 5:5 | Not explicitly by name in the verse evidence — the spirit vocabulary (ruach/pneuma) is not directly paired with love in the anchor verses in a way that names love as a spirit-level phenomenon. | OBS-103-T2-035 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Rom 5:5, Gal 5:22, Mat 22:37 | The Spirit-infusion evidence (Rom 5:5, OBS-103-126; Gal 5:22, OBS-103-128) points toward spirit-level origin in the sense of divine-Spirit origination — love's origin is the Holy Spirit's action, not the human spirit's generation. The commanded form ('you shall love' — Mat 22:37) places love at the will level, which in the programme's framework operates at or near the spirit boundary. Chesed as covenantal faithfulness — the mode that persists regardless of feeling — has a spirit-character quality: it operates at the deepest stable-disposition level rather than the feeling-fluctuating soul level. The sb_classification 'Spirit-Soul Interface' captures this: love has its deepest origin and most stable form at the spirit level but is also experienced at the soul level. The evidence implies spirit-level origin without explicitly naming it. |
| OBS-103-T2-036 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Lam 3:22, Pro 3:3, Mat 22:37 | If spirit-level location is confirmed (the inference from Q&A-038, if not explicitly stated), it would reveal that: (a) love is the deepest possible inner-being orientation — not surface emotion but foundational directedness; (b) love cannot be fully explained by the soul's affective fluctuations — chesed persists through feeling-states (Lam 3:22, OBS-103-088); (c) love is constitutionally prior to the acts and emotions it produces. | OBS-103-T2-042 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Joh 15:15, Phili 4:8, Hos 6:6, Jer 31:34 | Mind-engagement reveals that love has a genuine cognitive dimension — it is not sub-cognitive. | OBS-103-T2-043 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Mat 22:37, Mat 5:44, Rut 3:10, Mat 10:37 | Yes — emphatically. Enemy-love (Mat 5:44, OBS-103-143) is the clearest evidence: loving enemies requires volitional engagement against natural preference. The ranking of loves (Mat 10:37, OBS-103-151) requires a deliberate choice-act — placing love of Christ above natural love of family. Ruth's chesed (Rut 3:10, OBS-103-089) — choosing the elderly Boaz over young men — is love expressed through will against self-interest. The will's engagement is not peripheral but central to love in its highest form (agapē, chesed). The affective forms (phileō, dod) may be less volitionally constituted, but the command-forms require the will. |
| OBS-103-T2-044 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Mat 5:44, Joh 14:15, Joh 21:17, Rut 3:10 | Both operate in the data — love both requires and produces will-acts. It produces will-acts: love of Christ produces commandment-keeping (Joh 14:15, OBS-103-140) — the inner orientation generates the volitional pattern of life. The two modes are distinct: love-as-act-of-will (requiring deliberate engagement) vs love-as-generator-of-will (the inner orientation that produces volitional patterns). Both are evidenced. The affective forms (phileō, dod) may operate without explicit volitional initiation, but they too produce will-acts (Peter's fileō generates faithful mission-response, Joh 21:17, OBS-103-153). |

| OBS-103-T2-049 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Mat 22:37, Song 5:6, Pro 3:3, Phili 4:8 | Love is the programme's most fully integrated constitutional characteristic. The integration: at the spirit/will level — love is commanded (Mat 22:37), covenantal (chesed), and willed (enemy-love, Mat 5:44); at the soul level — love is experienced (Song 5:6 — soul failing at beloved's absence), given (Joh 15:13 — soul laid down for friends), and constitutive of identity (nephesh of God has a beloved, Jer 12:7); at the heart level — love is inscribed (Pro 3:3), infused by the Spirit (Rom 5:5), and the seat of love-awareness (Song 5:2); at the mind level — love requires and produces knowledge (Joh 15:15, Hos 6:6), and directs cognitive attention to the lovely (Phili 4:8); at the body level — love is expressed through kiss, embrace, tears, the movement of inner organs (Unit 7 multiple instances). No constitutional level is absent from the love vocabulary. Love is the programme's most constitutionally comprehensive characteristic — it operates at all levels simultaneously. |
| OBS-103-T2-050 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Rom 5:5, Luk 15:20, Lam 3:22, Pro 3:3 | Yes — the data evidences downward constitutional movement (from spirit-source into soul and body) as the primary direction. The movement is consistently from the interior (spirit/heart) outward (soul/affect, then body/act). | OBS-103-T2-051 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Rom 5:5, Zep 3:17, Luk 15:20, 1Pe 5:14 | The pattern from the data: divine love (Spirit-sourced) → enters heart (Rom 5:5) → produces soul-response (rest, joy, grief) → expresses bodily (kiss, embrace, tears, running). The sequence is: reception-at-depth → emergence-in-feeling → expression-in-body. This is the programme's first evidenced downward constitutional movement sequence for any characteristic. The intermediate soul-level is confirmed by OBS-103-041 and OBS-103-062 (Song) — love is experienced at the soul level before it expresses bodily. The body-level expression follows the soul-level experience: grief in the soul produces tears in the body; compassion-movement in the inner organs produces running and embrace. Pattern summary: Spirit origin → heart reception → soul experience → body expression. |
| OBS-103-T2-052 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Mat 5:44, Lam 3:22 | Will-engagement reveals that love in the biblical data is not reducible to feeling — it is a chosen orientation that the person actively maintains and directs. Enemy-love (Mat 5:44, OBS-103-143) is the most demanding evidence: love directed against natural antipathy requires the will's deliberate and sustained engagement. This reveals that love has depth precisely at the point where feeling runs out — chesed persists when feeling does not (Lam 3:22, OBS-103-088). The will is love's constitutional ground when affective experience is withdrawn or absent. This is the programme's key distinguishing feature for love versus mere positive feeling: love can sustain itself volitionally when the soul-level affective experience is absent. |
| OBS-103-T2-053 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Lam 3:22, Mat 5:44, Zep 3:17, Joh 11:36 | Love is not primarily emotional in the biblical data, though it has a rich emotional dimension. The evidence positions love as primarily dispositional/constitutional — an inner orientation that produces emotional states rather than consisting in them. Chesed is the clearest evidence: it persists without depending on emotional states (Lam 3:22 — 'the steadfast love of the Lord never ceases' despite Israel's devastating judgment). Agapē of enemies (Mat 5:44) operates where positive feeling is absent or where it must overcome negative feeling. The emotional states (joy, grief, rest, yearning) are love's products and evidence, not its constitutive substance. If love were primarily emotional, its commanded form ('you shall love') would be incoherent — emotions cannot be commanded. The commanded form confirms that love's primary operation is dispositional-volitional; the emotional dimension is real but secondary. |

Memory functions as love's sustaining faculty: love that cannot remember the beloved cannot maintain itself through absence or failure. |
| OBS-103-T2-061 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Psa 27:13, Jer 31:3, Song 2:16 | Yes. Psa 27:13 (OBS-103-080): 'I believe that I shall look upon the goodness of the Lord in the land of the living' — the psalmist's forward vision of God's love/goodness sustains the present inner life. The love-vocabulary consistently generates forward orientation (OBS-103-006, Q&A-006 — eschatological trajectory of love). Jer 31:3 (OBS-103-093): 'I have loved you with an everlasting love' — the everlasting qualifier generates an imagined future of permanent love. Song 2:16 (OBS-103-061): 'my beloved is mine' — the possession formula is also anticipatory: the belovedness extends into the imagined future. Imagination engages as love's visionary faculty — projecting the love-relationship into the future and sustaining the present through that projection. |
| OBS-103-T2-062 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Isa 5:1, Song 2:16, Luk 7:38 | Indirectly evidenced. The Song of Songs is love's most concentrated creative expression in Scripture — a poem whose entire form (extended metaphor, nature imagery, dialogue structure) is the creative vehicle of love-expression (OBS-103-041). Isa 5:1 (OBS-103-083): 'let me sing for my beloved my love song' — love generating song as creative expression. The kiss vocabulary (kiss = creative somatic expression of love) and the anointing (Luk 7:38, OBS-103-056) are body-as-creative-medium. However, the explicit creativity-faculty engagement (imagination deployed in artistic creation) is not named in the data — the creative dimension is inferred from the Song's form and from the love-song references. Partial: love generates creative expression in the data; explicit creativity-faculty engagement not directly named. |
| OBS-103-T2-063 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Song 5:6, Hos 6:6, Heb 12:16, Jer 31:20 | Yes — the desire-love boundary is analytically significant in the data. The dod and ahavah-intense vocabulary occupies the same semantic space as desire (R043 shares the ahav verbal root, OBS-103-022). Song 5:6 (OBS-103-062) — 'my soul failed me' — is desire-like in its intensity: the longing for the absent beloved. The yearning of God's inner parts (Jer 31:20, OBS-103-117) uses the same language-field as desire. Hos 6:6 (OBS-103-091): 'I desire (chaphets) steadfast love' — love becomes the object of God's desire. Heb 12:16 (OBS-103-078): Esau's appetite (trophe — food-desire) displacing love's covenantal inheritance is the paradigmatic desire-love conflict. The desire-faculty is love's closest adjacent faculty — love and desire share a mechanism (orientation toward an object) but are distinguished in the programme by the nature and stability of the commitment. |
| OBS-103-T2-064 | OBSERVATION | R103 love | Psa 16:11, Song 5:6, Zep 3:17 | Already fully addressed in T2.6 (Q&A-051, Q&A-052, Q&A-061). Love engages the affective faculty as its primary experiential medium — joy, grief, rest, delight, yearning, compassion-movement are love's affective palette. Love is not reducible to affective state (Q&A-061) but the affective faculty is love's most immediate experiential expression. The distinctive feature: love's affective range spans the widest spectrum in the programme — from the deepest joy (Psa 16:11) to the deepest grief (Song 5:6, 2Sa 1:26). Love is the affective faculty's governing characteristic. |
| OBS-103-T2-068 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Joh 13:34, Lam 3:22, Luk 15:20, Pro 3:3 | All three — building, sustaining, and restoring — are evidenced. Building: Joh 13:34 (OBS-103-145) — 'as I have loved you, you also are to love one another' — establishes the community as a new relational structure constituted by love. Sustaining: Lam 3:22 (OBS-103-088) — chesed that never ceases sustains the covenant relationship through judgment and desolation. Pro 3:3 (OBS-103-090) — heart-inscription sustains the disposition through circumstances. Restoring: Luk 15:20 (OBS-103-057) — the father's compassion-love restores the broken relationship with the returning son. Luk 7:47 (via SD-020): 'she loved much because she was forgiven much' — restored relationship (through forgiveness) produces love as its fruit. The restoration function: love does not merely sustain what exists but restores what has been broken — this is one of love's most structurally important capacities. |
| OBS-103-T2-069 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Jer 31:3, Joh 3:16, Rom 5:5, Eze 16:8 | The God-to-human direction is the programme's most evidentially dense directional axis for any characteristic. Four primary mechanisms: (a) **Covenantal declaration** — God names the love-relationship: 'I have loved you with an everlasting love' (Jer 31:3, OBS-103-093); 'you are the beloved of my soul' (Jer 12:7, OBS-103-086); 'This is my beloved Son' (Mat 3:17, OBS-103-120). The declaration is performative — it constitutes the relationship. (b) **Infusion** — God's love poured into hearts through the Spirit (Rom 5:5, OBS-103-126) — the Spirit as agent of love's transfer from divine to human inner being. (c) **Acts of love** — God gave his Son (Joh 3:16, OBS-103-141); God restores, forgives, compassionates (Lam 3:22, Isa 49:15, Jer 31:20). (d) **Covenantal covering** — Eze 16:8 (OBS-103-083b): God spreads his garment, makes a vow, enters covenant — the love-gift that constitutes the relationship. The overall pattern: divine love moves toward the human person through declaration, infusion, act, and covenant. |
| OBS-103-T2-070 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | 1Jo 4:19, Jer 31:3, Heb 13:5 | Divine love as gift has two structural features in the data: (a) **Priority** — 1Jo 4:19 ('we love because he first loved us') — divine love precedes all human love; it is not responsive to human merit but prior to it. Jer 31:3 ('with an everlasting love I have loved you') — the love predates the present moment and will outlast it. (b) **Sufficiency** — Heb 13:5 (OBS-103-138): the promise 'I will never leave you nor forsake you' is the ground for freedom from love-of-money — divine love is sufficient to displace the need for material security. The gift of divine love reorders the inner economy: receiving it makes other attachments unnecessary. As gift, divine love is both prior (unconditioned by merit) and sufficient (displacing rival loves by its own fullness). |
| OBS-103-T2-071 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Zep 3:17, Psa 16:11, Psa 127:2, Rom 1:7 | The receiver is constituted as agapētos (beloved) — an identity state, not merely a felt experience (OBS-103-040, OBS-103-122). The immediate inner-being state upon receiving divine love: rest/quieting (Zep 3:17, OBS-103-094); fullness and pleasure (Psa 16:11, OBS-103-112); soul-satisfaction (Jer 31:14, OBS-103-081). The sustained inner-being state: security ('I will never leave you' — Heb 13:5), known-ness ('Lord, you know everything — Joh 21:17, OBS-103-153), and free-from-striving (Psa 127:2, OBS-103-084). The person who receives divine love becomes the person who rests in it. The identity-state (beloved) and the experiential state (rest, fullness) are both dimensions of the receiver's inner condition. |
| OBS-103-T2-072 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Mat 22:37, Joh 14:15, Psa 63:3, Jer 2:2 | Human love toward God is the great commandment's content: love with all heart, soul, and mind (Mat 22:37, OBS-103-139). The data shows love toward God expressed through: (a) **Total mobilisation** — 'with all your heart and soul and mind' — no faculty withheld; (b) **Commandment-keeping** — 'if you love me, you will keep my commandments' (Joh 14:15, OBS-103-140) — love produces the obedience-pattern; (c) **Priority-ranking** — love of God above family love (Mat 10:37, OBS-103-151), above love of the present world (2Ti 4:10, OBS-103-148); (d) **Costly following** — Jer 2:2 (OBS-103-098) — Israel's early love expressed through following God into the wilderness; (e) **Praise** — Psa 63:3 (OBS-103-087): 'because your steadfast love is better than life, my lips will praise you' — love toward God expressed as praise. The human-to-God direction is constituted by total inner mobilisation, life-ordering, and expressive acts. |
| OBS-103-T2-073 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | 1Jo 4:19, 1Pe 1:22, 1Ti 6:10 | The condition for human love toward God is prior reception of divine love (1Jo 4:19 — 'we love because he first loved us'). Human love toward God is always responsive, not originating. The capacity required: soul-purification (1Pe 1:22, OBS-103-124) — the inner person must be cleared of the disordering loves that block genuine love toward God. The great commandment ('with all your soul') implies that the soul must be free from divided ultimate attachment to function as love-toward-God. Love of money (1Ti 6:10, OBS-103-132) and love of the world (2Ti 4:10, OBS-103-148) represent the prior conditions that prevent the human-to-God love-flow. The capacity for human love toward God is therefore: received divine love (enabling condition) + soul-purification from rival loves (clearing condition). |
| OBS-103-T2-074 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Psa 63:3, Joh 14:15, 1Pe 2:17, Hos 3:5 | The data gives several descriptions: (a) Psa 63:3 (OBS-103-087): the person who loves God so values chesed above life that praise becomes natural — the inner state is one of valuation so high it reorders the hierarchy of goods; (b) Joh 14:15 (OBS-103-140): the person who loves Christ keeps commandments — the inner state produces a habitual obedience-pattern; (c) 1Pe 2:17 (OBS-103-065): 'love the brotherhood, fear God' — love toward God and fear of God co-exist as the person's dual dispositional orientation toward the divine. Fear is not love's replacement but its companion. The inner state: reverent love, or loving reverence — the integration of love and fear that Hos 3:5 names ('come in fear to the Lord and to his goodness,' OBS-103-082). The person who loves God is also the person who properly fears God. |
| OBS-103-T2-075 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Joh 15:13, Mat 5:44, Lev 19:18, Rut 3:10 | Love as given outward is the primary ethical direction of the commandment structure: love your neighbour (Lev 19:18), love your enemy (Mat 5:44), love one another (Joh 13:34). The giving of love reaches its maximum in Joh 15:13 (OBS-103-125) — 'greater love has no one than this: that someone lay down his life/soul for his friends.' The gift of the soul is love's outer limit. The giving-forms span: chesed as daily covenantal faithfulness given to the covenant-partner (OBS-103-089); agapē given to the enemy against natural preference (OBS-103-143); phileō given as warmth within the community (OBS-103-119); rachamim given as compassion toward the suffering (OBS-103-105). Love-as-given is the primary ethical form in which the inner orientation is concretely actualised. |
| OBS-103-T2-076 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | 1Jo 4:19, Zep 3:17, Rom 1:7, Luk 15:20 | Love as received is constitutive of identity (agapētos, OBS-103-040), productive of rest (Zep 3:17, OBS-103-094), and the enabling condition for giving love (1Jo 4:19, OBS-103-146). The reception is: (a) constitutive — being named beloved by God constitutes who the person is; (b) enabling — divine love received is what makes human love possible (1Jo 4:19); (c) experiential — rest, fullness, and joy are the experiential register of received love. Reception of love is not passive — Song 5:2 (OBS-103-108) shows the beloved opening the door; Luk 15:20 (OBS-103-057) shows the son returning. Some movement toward the source appears to be the condition for reception (Q&A-031). |
| OBS-103-T2-077 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | 1Jo 4:19, Psa 127:2, Joh 3:19 | The data provides a distinction. True reception: 1Jo 4:19 — responsive love flows; the person who receives divine love loves in return. Psa 127:2 (OBS-103-084) — the beloved sleeps — reception produces rest and effortlessness. Jer 31:14 (OBS-103-081) — the soul is satisfied. Non-reception: Joh 3:19 (OBS-103-147) — those who encounter light-love do not receive it because their inner love-commitment runs the other way. The distinguishing feature: genuine reception of love produces love in return (1Jo 4:19) and produces rest/satisfaction (Psa 127:2). Non-reception while encountering: the person continues in the disordered love that blocked reception, unchanged and satisfied with it. The test of reception is: does love-received produce love-outward and rest-inward? If so, reception is genuine. If the person encounters the love-offer but remains oriented toward a rival love-object, reception has not occurred. |
| OBS-103-T2-078 | OBSERVATION | R103 love | Joh 3:19, 2Ti 4:10, Luk 16:14 | Already addressed at T1.7.3 (Q&A-033). The person who does not receive love is not loveless but misdirected — loving a wrong object. The inner state is commitment to the rival love that blocks reception. The person remains internally coherent (in their own economy of loves) but existentially misdirected. No additional evidence beyond Q&A-033. |
| OBS-103-T2-080 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Mat 12:50, Joh 13:35, Rom 12:10 | Human-to-human love creates a social architecture with three features: (a) **Restructured family** — Mat 12:50 (OBS-103-063): 'whoever does the will of my Father is my brother and sister and mother' — love redraws the family boundary around shared orientation toward God rather than natural kinship. (b) **Public community mark** — Joh 13:35 (OBS-103-129): mutual love is externally legible as the community's identity. The social architecture of love is publicly readable — it creates a community whose internal reality is visible to outsiders. (c) **Competitive generosity** — Rom 12:10 (OBS-103-119): 'outdo one another in showing honor' — love creates a social order where the competition is in giving rather than taking, in honour-showing rather than honour-claiming. These three features constitute a social architecture that is structurally counter to the natural social patterns of kinship, concealment, and rivalry. |
| OBS-103-T2-082 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | 1Jo 4:19, Rom 5:5, Tit 2:4, 1Pe 1:22 | Yes — multiple acquisition-pathways: (a) **Reception of divine love** — 1Jo 4:19 (OBS-103-146): human love is acquired by receiving divine love first. The primary acquisition pathway is reception, not self-generation. (b) **Spirit infusion** — Rom 5:5 (OBS-103-126): God's love poured into hearts through the Spirit — the Spirit is the agent of love's acquisition at the heart level. Gal 5:22 — love as the Spirit's fruit — love grows in the person as the Spirit produces it. (c) **Training** — Tit 2:4 (OBS-103-124 context): young women trained to love husbands and children — love as a domestically trainable virtue. (d) **Soul purification through obedience** — 1Pe 1:22 (OBS-103-124): obedience purifies the soul for sincere love. The obedience-pathway cleanses the inner person of what blocks love, enabling authentic love to emerge. (e) **Covenant-formation** — Pro 3:3: chesed written on the heart — love is inscribed through the practices of the covenant life. |
| OBS-103-T2-083 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | 1Th 3:12, Rut 3:10 | Yes — explicitly. 1Th 3:12 (OBS-103-130): 'may the Lord make you increase and abound in love' — love admits of increase; the Lord is the agent of its growth. The prayer-form implies that love's increase is both desirable and possible, dependent on the Lord's action. The degree-language in the data also implies growth: Rut 3:10 — 'you have made this last kindness greater than the first' — chesed measurably greater in a later act than an earlier one. Love is not fixed at a static level but admits of deepening expression and increase over time. |
| OBS-103-T2-084 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Joh 15:15, 1Pe 1:22, 1Cor 13:4-7 | Yes. Joh 15:15 (OBS-103-052): the disciples are transformed from servants to friends through Christ's love — a fundamental identity and relational reclassification. 1Pe 1:22 (OBS-103-124): soul-purification as the outcome of the love-formation process — the inner person is changed by the pathway that leads to sincere love. The 1Cor 13 trajectory (OBS-103-127): love's sustained exercise produces a character that does not envy, boast, or seek its own — the moral character is transformed by the practice of love. Luk 7:47 (via SD-020): the woman who loves much has been transformed by forgiveness — the transformation in her produced the love-expression. Love both requires and produces transformation. |
| OBS-103-T2-085 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | 2Ti 4:10, Jer 31:3, Lam 3:22, Joh 21:17 | The data shows love can be abandoned or displaced, but the covenantal-divine form (chesed, agapē) is presented as permanent. Human love: reversible. 2Ti 4:10 (OBS-103-148): Demas' love of Paul's community abandoned for love of the world — the human love-commitment can be redirected. Mat 10:37 (OBS-103-151) implies love-rankings can be disordered (natural love displacing love of Christ). Joh 21:17: Peter's love was contested but affirmed — the question of love's persistence through failure is the Joh 21 theme. Divine love: irreversible in character. Jer 31:3 (OBS-103-093): 'with an everlasting love' — the qualifier rules out reversibility for the divine instance. Lam 3:22 (OBS-103-088): 'chesed never ceases' — divine chesed is by definition permanent. The distinction: divine love as irreversible; human love as subject to redirection through competing love-allegiances. |
| OBS-103-T2-086 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | 1Jo 4:19, Rom 5:5, 1Pe 1:22, Tit 2:4 | The primary mechanism from the data: divine love received → responsive love generated (1Jo 4:19). The Spirit is the operating agent of this mechanism (Rom 5:5, Gal 5:22) — the Spirit infuses divine love into the heart, which produces the inner reorientation toward love. The soul-purification mechanism (1Pe 1:22): obedience → purification → sincere love — a preparatory clearing that enables love to emerge. The training mechanism (Tit 2:4): repeated practice within the community forms love as a stable disposition. The forgiveness-trigger mechanism (Luk 7:47 — via SD-020): received forgiveness generates love as its fruit. Together: love's mechanism operates at multiple levels — the Spirit as the primary agent, obedience as the clearing condition, practice as the formation pathway, and received forgiveness as a specific love-trigger. |
| OBS-103-T2-087 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Jer 31:34, 1Th 3:12, Psa 16:11 | The data presents love as eschatologically oriented toward perfection and direct knowledge. Jer 31:34 (OBS-103-072): the new covenant vision — love of neighbour is superseded by direct divine knowledge; the mediated form of love (teaching the neighbour about God) gives way to the direct form. 1Jo 4:18 (via SP-103-029): perfect love casts out fear — 'perfect love' is an eschatological state that eliminates the inner-being disturbance of fear. 1Th 3:12 (OBS-103-130): love abounds toward the Lord's coming — love is moving toward a fullness coinciding with the eschatological event. Psa 16:11 (OBS-103-112): 'pleasures forevermore' at God's right hand — the eschatological fullness of the love-relationship is pleasures without end. The trajectory: love is currently partial (partial knowledge, partial reception) and is moving toward perfection (direct knowledge, perfect love, eternal pleasure in God's presence). |
| OBS-103-T2-088 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Joh 13:34, 1Pe 1:22, 1Jo 4:19 | Yes — fundamentally. Love cannot be formed in isolation: it requires a beloved to be directed toward. The community formation of love (Joh 13:34 — 'love one another'; filadelfia cultivated together; training in Tit 2:4 within a community context) is inherently relational. The primary formation-by-others: reception of divine love as the enabling condition (1Jo 4:19) — God's action toward the person is the formative ground. The community of mutual love (1Pe 1:22 — 'sincere brotherly love' developed through shared obedience) is a communal-formation context. Love cannot be a solo formation project — it requires the other's presence, action, and response. The relational structure of love (always toward another) makes community the necessary formation context. |
| OBS-103-T2-089 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Pro 3:3, Psa 4:3 | T2.8 identified the heart-inscription (Pro 3:3) as a partial deposit-candidate — metaphorical but not fully confirmed as a constitutional body-deposit. If the heart-inscription is treated as a deposit: the consequence is that love becomes a stable constitutional feature of the person rather than a fluctuating state — chesed written on the heart is love that endures through circumstance. The heart-inscription consequence: the person whose heart has love inscribed acts from love habitually, not only when feeling love. This is consistent with the chasid profile (OBS-103-026): the godly person whose inner character is shaped by covenantal love. The inscription makes love a character-quality rather than a feeling-event. Gap: the full body-deposit question remains partially evidenced; this response reflects the heart-inscription's probable consequence if it is a deposit, not a fully confirmed answer. |
| OBS-103-T2-090 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Pro 3:3, Psa 4:3 | Per the heart-inscription evidence (Pro 3:3, OBS-103-090): the inscription of love on the heart implies a lasting constitutional change — the person whose heart has chesed written into it is a different person constitutionally from the one who merely performs loving acts occasionally. The chasid (OBS-103-026) is defined as a person-type, not merely a person-doing-things — the love-character is constitutive of who they are. However, the evidence for permanent constitutional change in the biological-body sense (as distinct from the character-level) is not directly stated. The character-change appears lasting; the somatic-deposit sense remains uncertain. |
| OBS-103-T2-091 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Exo 34:6, Gal 5:22, Mat 22:37 | Top co-occurrences from §5 data (OBS-103-042 through OBS-103-051): R023 compassion (196), R187 strength (105), R197 authority (69), R117 peace (68), R059 faith (62), R044 despair (55), R112 mind (52), R173 will (52), R019 calling (51), R182 Soul (50), R043 desire (49), R051 distress (49), R183 heart (47). The pattern reveals three structural clusters: (a) **Love's relational cluster** — compassion (23), peace (117), kindness (99), mercy (111) — love co-occurs with its closest relational companions within C17, confirming cluster integrity; (b) **Love's constitutional cluster** — soul (182), heart (183), mind (112) — love is present in verses that name the inner constitutional locations; (c) **Love's theological cluster** — faith (59), calling (19), covenant (34) — love co-occurs consistently with the programme's foundational theological vocabulary. The surprise: strength (105) and authority (197) are co-occurrence #2 and #3 — love and power are structurally co-present in the data at high frequency. |
| OBS-103-T2-092 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | 1Cor 13:1-3, Lam 3:22, Luk 7:47 | Three surprising co-occurrences: (a) **Strength (R187, 105) and authority (R197, 69)** — love and power as the second and third highest co-occurrence registers. This is analytically unexpected — strength and authority are C20 cluster characteristics, not C17. The data suggests that love and power are not merely adjacent but structurally co-present in biblical contexts. The 1Cor 13 framework places love above gifts of power ('tongues of angels, gifts of prophecy') — the comparison implies they occupy the same evidential terrain. SD-026 (already raised) addresses this. (b) **Despair (R044, 55)** — despair appearing in the top 10 co-occurrences with love. The lament/petition pattern (despair crying to love for rescue) generates this co-occurrence. Love and despair are structurally linked as the inner state that appeals to love and the love that responds to despair. (c) **Guilt (R073, 32)** — less surprising given SD-028 (forgiveness-love chain) but notable that guilt appears in the top 25 — love and guilt are structurally related at the verse level through the forgiveness-love causal chain. |
| OBS-103-T2-093 | OBSERVATION | R103 love | N/A (structural assessment) | The co-occurrence pattern confirms the Relational Disposition primary dimension. Love co-occurs most densely with: compassion (the compassionate form of relational orientation), peace (the relational-outcome), faith (the trust-orientation toward God), calling (identity constituted relationally), and the soul/heart/mind (the constitutional locations of relational experience). This is the pattern expected for a Relational Disposition characteristic. The strength/authority co-occurrence adds texture (love operates in contexts of power) but does not complicate the primary classification — love remains relational disposition even when co-present with power vocabulary. |
| OBS-103-T2-094 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | 1Jo 4:19, Joh 14:15, Gal 5:22, 1Ti 6:10 | The data is unusually rich in love's sequential relationships. Love as effect (something precedes it): (a) Received divine love → human love (1Jo 4:19, OBS-103-146); (b) Forgiveness received → love expressed (Luk 7:47, via SD-020); (c) Obedience → soul purification → sincere love (1Pe 1:22, OBS-103-124); (d) Spirit infusion → love in heart (Rom 5:5, OBS-103-126). Love as cause (love produces): (e) Love of God → commandment-keeping (Joh 14:15, OBS-103-140); (f) Love → all other Spirit-fruits (Gal 5:22, OBS-103-128 — if love is generative); (g) Love of money → craving → departure from faith → anguish (1Ti 6:10, OBS-103-132 — the disordered sequence); (h) Perfect love → displacement of fear (1Jo 4:18, via SP-103-029). The sequential data reveals love as both deeply downstream of divine action and richly upstream of the ethical and moral life. Love is the programme's most central sequential node. |
| OBS-103-T2-095 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Gal 5:22, 1Cor 13:13, 1Jo 4:19, Joh 14:15 | Love appears to occupy a **mediating and generative** position in the programme's sequential architecture. Mediating: it stands between received divine love (prior) and the ethical-moral life (subsequent). It is not the origin (God is the origin) but it is the indispensable middle — without love, no commandment-keeping, no Spirit-fruit, no community-identity. Generative: love heads the fruit-of-Spirit list (Gal 5:22) and defines the measure of all subsequent virtues (1Cor 13:13 — 'the greatest is love'). Love functions as the programme's organising characteristic at the ethical level: it is what the other Spirit-fruits emerge from and what the commandments resolve into. This is consistent with the registry description ('most foundational word') and DIM-103-001's call to map love's governing position relative to other characteristics. |
| OBS-103-T2-096 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Psa 16:11, Zep 3:17, Song 5:6, Joh 14:15 | Yes — love is causally productive in the data at both the inner-being and the social levels: (a) **Love → joy** (Psa 16:11, OBS-103-112): love-in-God's-presence produces fullness of joy; (b) **Love → rest** (Zep 3:17, OBS-103-094): God's love produces inner quieting; (c) **Love → grief** (Song 5:6, OBS-103-062; 2Sa 1:26, OBS-103-095): love under loss produces grief — love constitutes the grief by making the beloved's absence unbearable; (d) **Love → obedience** (Joh 14:15, OBS-103-140): love of Christ produces commandment-keeping; (e) **Love → praise** (Psa 63:3, OBS-103-087): love expressed as response to chesed-above-life produces praise. Love does not merely accompany these states but appears to constitute or cause them. It is the programme's most causally productive characteristic. |
| OBS-103-T2-097 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Gal 5:22, Luk 7:47, Luk 15:20 | From the data: (a) Love may constitute or generate all Spirit-fruits (Gal 5:22, Q&A-105) — if love is the single fruit of which joy, peace, patience, etc. are expressions, then love partially constitutes those characteristics. (b) Forgiveness may constitute the condition from which love emerges (Luk 7:47 via SD-020) — if 'she loved because she was forgiven much,' forgiveness is constitutive of the love-response. (c) Compassion and love appear to be constitutively related — compassion may be love's form under the condition of the other's suffering (OBS-103-042, OBS-103-057). Gap: the precise constitutive relationships between love and compassion, mercy, kindness cannot be fully determined from Stage 2a evidence alone — these require Session D treatment. Partial: love-as-constituent-of-Spirit-fruits and forgiveness-as-constituent-of-love-response are the best-evidenced claims. |

| OBS-103-T2-100 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | N/A (structural assessment) | Vocabulary sharing at this density reveals that love is not a bounded standalone characteristic but the semantic centre of a vocabulary cluster. The characteristics surrounding love (compassion, mercy, kindness, goodness, desire, peace) share vocabulary with it because they are all expressions or dimensions of a common inner-being reality — oriented-attachment-to-the-good-and-to-persons. The registries do not name wholly distinct phenomena; they name distinguishable aspects of a single broadly relational inner-being reality. The practical implication: Session D synthesis for love cannot treat the other C17 characteristics as merely adjacent — they are lexically and conceptually continuous with love. | OBS-103-T2-101 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Lam 3:22, Isa 49:15, Luk 15:20 | The closest adjacent characteristic from co-occurrence data is compassion (R023, 196 shared verses). What distinguishes them from the data: compassion is love's responsive form under the condition of the other's suffering — the rachamim/womb-movement is activated by the beloved's need or distress. Love without suffering context does not require the racham-movement; love in the presence of suffering always produces it. Stated differently: compassion is the subset of love that is suffering-triggered; love is the broader orientation of which compassion is one mode (OBS-103-029, OBS-103-042). However: the data does not fully distinguish chesed from compassion at the verse level — both can be present simultaneously (Lam 3:22). The distinction is partial. | OBS-103-T2-102 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Lam 3:22, Exo 34:6 | The racham/chesed overlap at Lam 3:22 ('his chesed never ceases, his rachamim never come to an end') is the programme's clearest example of the boundary difficulty — the two terms are paired in parallel without distinction. At the definitional level the boundary is: chesed = covenantal-faithful love (disposition of the covenant partner); rachamim = compassion-love (response to suffering). But at the verse level they co-occur so consistently that their experiential separation is unclear. Gap: the boundary is analytically drawn but evidentially porous. | OBS-103-T2-103 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Lam 3:22, Isa 49:15 | Between love and compassion: the distinction appears to be one of **trigger** rather than degree, kind, direction, or constitutional level. Both are inner dispositions of orientation toward another (same kind, same direction, similar constitutional level). What differs is the activating condition: compassion is triggered by the other's suffering; love can be present without suffering. This makes them the same characteristic differently activated, rather than different characteristics. This reading is consistent with SD-007 (compassion as love-responding-to-suffering hierarchy). However, the data does not definitively confirm this — it is an analytical interpretation of the co-occurrence and definitional data. Deferred to Session D for resolution. |

| OBS-103-T2-109 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Lam 3:22, Song 2:16, Isa 49:15, 1Cor 13:4 | Primary Hebrew terms and root meanings: **chesed** (H2617A) — root implies binding loyalty, covenant-fidelity; possibly related to the idea of steadfastness or bending toward; the most theologically laden term in the OT love vocabulary. **ahavah** (H0160) — root ahav (to breathe after, to desire) — implying love as a form of directed longing or desire. **racham** (H7355) / **rachamim** (H7356B) — root rechem (womb) — love as womb-like envelopment and tender compassion; the most somatically grounded root. **dod** (H1730G/H) — root unclear; used for lover/beloved in the Song — the erotic-relational vocabulary. Primary Greek terms: **agapē** (G0026) / **agapaō** (G0025) — of uncertain pre-classical etymology; LXX/NT coinage whose meaning is constituted by Scripture rather than importing a prior secular meaning (OBS-103-016). **phileō** (G5368) / **philia** (G5373) / **filos** (G5384) — root from philos (friend); classical Greek for natural affectionate love. Root meanings together reveal: love spans willed-covenant (chesed), longing-desire (ahavah), somatic-compassion (racham), erotic-beloved (dod), self-giving-willed (agapē), and natural-affection (phileō). |
| OBS-103-T2-110 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Mat 22:37, 1Cor 13:13, Rom 1:7, Rom 5:5 | Taking agapaō/agapē as the primary NT term: **agapaō** (verb, 344 occurrences) — love as an action, exercisable and commandable; the verbal form affirms love's volitional dimension. **agapē** (noun, 133 occurrences) — love as an entity, a reality that can be 'poured into hearts' (Rom 5:5), that 'never fails' (1Cor 13:8), that is the greatest (1Cor 13:13). **agapētos** (adjective/participle, 79 occurrences) — beloved, the passive recipient of love; love as constituting an identity-state in the object. Together: verb + noun + adjective-participle spans the full grammatical range: love as act (verb), love as reality/quality (noun), and love as identity-constitutive state (adjective). This three-part grammatical range confirms Q&A-016's finding that love is simultaneously act, disposition, and condition. For chesed: primarily noun (covenant-quality) with verbal cognate (chasad — to act with chesed) — the noun-primary form confirms love as a stable quality before it is an act. |
| OBS-103-T2-111 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Joh 3:16, Mat 5:44, Joh 3:19, Psa 63:3 | Agapē's semantic range in the NT evidence: (a) divine love for humanity (Joh 3:16); (b) human love for God (Mat 22:37); (c) mutual love in community (Joh 13:34); (d) love of enemy (Mat 5:44); (e) disordered love (love of darkness — Joh 3:19; love of the world — 2Ti 4:10; love of the pre-eminent position — 3Jo 9). The semantic range spans divine, human-covenantal, communal, and misdirected forms. Chesed's range: divine faithfulness, human loyalty, the person-type (chasid), the failure of chesed (withdrawal, demand). The combined semantic range of the primary terms covers the full moral landscape — from the highest (God's love as his being) to the lowest (love misdirected toward darkness). This breadth is unique in the programme — no other characteristic has primary terms whose semantic range spans from the ontologically highest (divine nature) to the morally inverted (love of darkness). |
| OBS-103-T2-112 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Lam 3:22, Jer 12:7, Psa 4:3, Joh 15:13 | Yes — the vocabulary structure itself distinguishes these: **Disposition vs act**: agapē (noun — disposition) vs agapaō (verb — act); chesed (noun — the quality) vs chasad (verb — to act with chesed). **Received vs given**: agapētos (passive — received) vs agapaō (active — given); 'beloved of my soul' (Jer 12:7, received by Israel) vs 'I have loved you' (Jer 31:3, given by God). **Condition vs quality**: the lover-as-identity (chasid as person-type, OBS-103-026; filos as person-type, OBS-103-018) names the quality that has become a stable condition; the act-forms name love as an exercised capacity. The vocabulary is architecturally precise — it distinguishes what love is (quality/disposition), what love does (act), who love comes from (given), who love is directed toward (received), and who love constitutes (condition/identity). |
| OBS-103-T2-115 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Psa 63:3, Lam 3:22, Hos 3:5 | The data contains supplication-for-love contexts but not a dedicated seeking term. | OBS-103-T2-116 | THEOLOGICAL_NOTE | R103 love | Joh 3:16, Lam 3:22, Psa 63:3 | The key LXX observation from the data: the LXX translators used agapē/agapaō to translate both ahav and chesed, embedding the Hebrew covenantal sense of steadfast love into the Greek agapē vocabulary. This is historically significant — agapē in the NT carries the weight of the OT chesed through the LXX translation. When the NT says 'God so loved (ēgapēsen)' (Joh 3:16), it uses the term that the LXX used for God's chesed toward Israel. Continuity is established at the lexical level: the NT's agapē is not a new concept but the Hebrew chesed in Greek form.
